O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the final word on medical science together with its explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with this surgery, which is the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And for this reason that the work of hands is practiced in our region and is taken from all over everywhere, it is because it is a difficult science and a demanding art, and there is no delay in its force except for the small descriptions in books of ancient times that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed up and science is remote.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can give it new life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of the iron tools of cauterization, and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of it, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for this reason the art of surgery has been neglected in our country because there are no good surgeons.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in it must master the science of anatomy as Galileo says, as far as he knows the shape and connection and separation of the bones, and has knowledge of the muscles and nerves and joints and the number of bones, and the movement and flowing veins and resting veins, and their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates said that the right hand is not like the left, nor is the work like the hand, and most of all in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that if one does not know the things mentioned above, he must be careful not to make mistakes and not learn from experience; so I have often seen many of those who engage in this science and abandon themselves to theory and speculation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess on the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries in the neck; so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he brought out a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also seen it said that if you treat the patient properly, the condition of the patient and the size of the stone are well-known, and he would certainly die if treated this way.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who caught a duch of our land who had a broken leg, and with the breaking he got a wound; and the foolish doctor, out of ignorance, cut the break close to the wound with a sharp knife, leaving no scar on the wound, and left it so; and commanded that he not remove it; and delayed it so that the leg was completely mangled and the foot was lost in the end.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to bring the leg out; and when I took it out he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways that the member is corrupted are already confirmed, and cannot be healed; and the corruption does not cease to spread through the member as long as the members are completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder which will destroy the abscess and putrefaction, and then inflame by the evil of its mastery.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is purred out with melancholic humor, one must touch it with iron if it is in the right place so that one can completely destroy what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this, trachy filz, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, where there is danger and fear in many things; and I will show in each of these chapters in this book where there is peril and fear.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For if you keep this in mind, so that the foolish gaze cannot speak ill of you; If you take your weapons in agreement, and attack your diseases lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are delivered; and leave behind the expected diseases of grief health; And hold your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiée provided some of his advice thus: "Do not take on yourself the care of a bad disease, lest you be called foolish.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and medicinal water, and the following chapters are ordered from the top down to the bottom, and the shapes of instruments, and the ironing tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about tailoring and piercing, suction cups and wounds, extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and torquing, and similar things; and it is ordered that the heads of the screws be smooth, and the forms of instruments be laid out.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, as we remember the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of the aid and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the most distant word, subtile science, and secret answers; and many wise men would speak about it, and agree with what I say; and I am short of words because I shorten the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that universal aid cauterizes all colors having matter, except for two types of color: that is to say, hot color with matter and dry color with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together matter, some devised and said that cautery is great help; and another said the opposite: that cautery does not deserve to be sick of heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and must not be cured by hot disease from heat, nor from dryness; and he who says that cautery does great help to the hot and dry disease which comes in courses to men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never once by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all way, nothing but fire enters into it save he who has tried it, and knows by long practice the character of the ointment of cautery, and the differences in the complexions of men, their dispositions, and causes of their diseases, and also the seasons; for we fear not any other complexion, even if it be cold or moist, in diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the hair should grow together and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery is more effective if it causes discharge of cure, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member unless by chance.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines come from one member to another by spreading, and bring about the malady of healing; and by chance fire, because of its height and because of its substance's goodness, does not do this unless there is surplus.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And which I have found by experiment and through the long service and study that I have put into this art, and is based on the truth of things; and therefore I beg your pardon for the length of speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret of what has been found out about fire, and the quality of the work, how it defeats diseases of bodies, as the philosopher says in his demonstration; receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that these cauterizations should be made at a certain time, and let them be prayed.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is fitting in all seasons, for by the aid of the cauterization the impending harm is prevented; and most importantly, the cauterization is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the season when greater ill may come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, son, as they do in the field; for to the illness that is healed by cauterization there is no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they believe, because cauterization is nothing more than a medicine that changes the color, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is more efficacious than medicine in terms of haste in its effect, and for its virtue and majesty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And there are times when the disease comes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and useless things are gathered within him by acquiring flesh and similar things, unless cauterization is administered in which he has a little superfluity and moisture, as cauterizing thickly because of the pain, and similar things, and that part of the pain does not return again but it occurs a little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand at all because cauterization is called the tears of medicine, and that's it; but they don't believe that cauterization is worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and cauterization is the tears of medicine for this reason that whenever we administered ways to treat diseases in any disease they do not deserve, therefore let us administer cauterization, and it deserves.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, open well that cauterization is the tears of medicine, not at all according to the intentions of the foolish.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Li ancien dirent que cauteres d'estrument d'or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualitet de l'or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n'est mie ver car je l'ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c'est ver en aucuns homes; et cauteres d'or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	The ancient ones said that gold instruments for cauterizing are more effective than those of iron, and they only mentioned the qualities of gold and its high purity because of its effect on healing; They said that the heat from gold instruments does not cause inflammation, but this is not true as I have proven it, for I found that in some cases it can cause inflammation; And gold cauterizing tools are more effective than iron, as they claim. However, when you heat a gold instrument, it does not take long to cool down; and if you heat it too much, it will burn in the fire, and thus there is sufficient prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	For I have ordered you this chapter of the treatment of the eye, since it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Or aultre ai ordeneit de cautere de la peitrine comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	And for this I have ordered fire cautery for the head, which should be applied to the patient so that the hair remains long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them still so they do not move until they grow. This cauterization is useful in case of moisture and cold on the head, and because of many humors that descend from the hair and ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain of teeth and pain of throat, and most especially for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis and soda and apoplexia and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a solution medicine which cleanses the head III or IIII, according to what the virtues and the ease and the habit of the patient can bear; and then do again the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then do sit the crosswise between your hands, and put his hands on his neck; after place the root of your two palms on the root of his neck between his II hairs; and let come your two hands, if it bleeds from then then heat the cautery which is called "olive", by which this form is:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the signet of ink, and do going down and extract your hand pokey and poky returning; then let your hand alone, and reward the place where you see the bone I small; and if you don't see it, then continue the cautery as long as you see the bone like I told you; after take I piece of string, and put in weep and cotton, and put on the mark, and let it be for so long that the heating is done; then cure the wound with an ointment which is called "tetrafarmacon" until it is well.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And said the old man, that the longer the wound is open, the more it bleeds; and for this reason if it is moved.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said none of these that one must let the cautery burn as much of the bone as possible, and then mend what is burned of the bone, and be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And said another that one must let the cautery burn as high as possible, and then push it so hard that the humors come out of the bone; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after which one must mend and heal.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of burning do not seem good to me in all cases, except for some people where it is possible to fear; and I think that I should leave it open, because the head is weakened by continuous nature solutions, as we witness with other limbs; and even if the head of the sick is weak from nature, and the first cauterization seems more safe and soft to me, and I use it in such a way that it heals.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of old age pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all the head comes chronic pain and lasts for a long time, then use herbal remedies and pills that are called "cochier", and head cooling and oils and poultices; and if one makes the fire cautery which we have just mentioned, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient is of a strong nature, and is not too cold; then apply the fire cautery as described above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making the fire cautery over each hair of the head up to the bone, as we have just said, and making a hole where one calls it "vasselz"; and set the ventuse; and adjust your hand so that you do not see it up to the bone: the patient feels too much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it elsewhere; and it is good that fire cauterizes over each hair of the head are smaller than those over which one cauterizes the skin of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head there is sudden pain, and it extends to the oil, and the headache has been cured with medicines that are contrary to water, and all else has failed: then let the fire cauterization be done according to two ways, that is to say, with aqueous medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cautery of aqueous medicine: that is to say, you squeeze a date of aloes and remove the peel and the core in two pieces like the head, and then you place it on the temple or at the root where the pain is, in such a way that you can dip the aloes in wax; and when it has been dipped, leave it there for twelve hours; and then take it off and treat with an aloes date, and leave the wound for two or three days; and then put cotton soaked in oil over it until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the healing process as long as he is healthy; and if you see any of the medicines I have written about in this chapter on burning medicines, take them as directed.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if done like this.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "close" because the head is made in the form of a clo or it has I hole of a corbeur, and middle to a small appearance; and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the fire a little bit, until the halfway of the keur (bone) is burned; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is further away, and runs a lot of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that put cotton in the form of thread, and place it on the spot for three days; then dip the cotton in oil, and then heal the spot with the healing process as long as he is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer called "cultellare", all over the tip, and be careful not to seal the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	for headaches: When you treat headaches as we have said before in the division of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cautery described at the beginning of this medicine and the iron does not help him; therefore it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and so sign on the sore spot a line half a inch long, and hold your hand once, and lift it up so that you do not cover the artery and do not come up to the bone; and guard against the mandible that moves when you stretch, and let the rest remain as it is, and that spasms do not come to the disease, and guard against the escape of blood from the artery when it is covered, or if it has escaped, there is great fear and most of all to those who do not know it, and who are students and untested; and let the work remain in its place; but I will tell you how to stop headaches when the artery is blocked, and I will show you at what point it hurts in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteurs do not suffice to the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him with fire at the head as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautores that we have said or the chapitre of extraction of the artery, with the cauteur that has II knives; and this cauteur is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold weather
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ears from cold weather, and one has applied giải độc và các phương pháp điều trị khác như chúng ta đã nói trong phần phân chia, và cơn đau không thuyên giảm, thì hãy sử dụng loại lửa gọi là 'poins', hình dạng của nó như sau:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have made the whole ear that is sore, or the two sides, where there is pain, warm up with fire a little distance from the root of the ear then, as you have marked the place, make X points in each ear; after that, cure the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	that must be cured by fire is only for those that move with fluid, as we have said in the division of diseases; and not to make fire for similar things that come from heat and salt of the sea.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this torture of the mouth that moves with fluid from sea water and sputum from the throat and gargling, and it is not worth it, then you must make three fire treatments: one at the root of the ear, another a little further forward on the temple, and the third between the two lips; and place the fire in the healthy part, and let the fire burn halfway through; and this is the form of the fire treatment:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the appearance of the scalpel that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and needs the blade to be a little thicker; after healing the place as I have said above, as long as it remains healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then do IV cauterizations: II on the II horns of the head, and I cut off the head, and I apply the vessel as we have said before, and the after-cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be cured as we have said above.
de litargie	of lime
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient many years and pills to clean out the brain; after cutting off the head of the patient completely, and placing on the occipital lobe thyme extract which is written or used to make plasters; and that is the way of the cauterization: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is well thus far, it is good; and if not, he shall have three fire cauteries to the top of his head, descending to the collar, and leaving space between each cautery two inches wide; and the cure as for the others, and if you see him jerking, and the patient suffers, then a fire cautery in the middle; and it is necessary, two others on the two horns, and the cure until he is well; and be the cauteries which are called "olivare," as I have said above.
de la froidor dou chief	Of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be washed with water and with what we have said above; after that, the doctor should wash the patient's head, then he shall make a fire cautery to the top of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three in the middle of the back of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers and the disease persists, then he shall make four fire cauteries on the spine of the back; and he shall leave it until the first cure is burned, and lower his hand; after that, the cure until he is well, and be the cauteries which are called "olivare" as we have said above.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	of epilepsy One should use fire cautery only for those who are febrile, and first to irrigate the brain and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section on treatment when the patient is great and suffering from feverish medicines.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If it is a child who cannot endure the fire, let him gargle and chew, irrigating the brain often with good meat; then let him lie down in the middle, and let him be cauterized according to what we have said above, and cauterize his neck, and each of his horns; and if the patient is parched and suffering, let him be cauterized as I have said before to those who are paralyzed and have a softening of the back and neck, and let the cauterization be with olive oil according to the way I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is infected, make a fire cautery using this method.
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excesses or corrupted moisture and thick pus, then make half fire cautery as we have said to the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy there is decline of excesses to melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then he should drink something that will clear the brain, according to what we have said in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After re-establishing the head of the patient; after making a well-formed turban out of linen, also as a circle, put it on the head; and let the patient sit with his back supported and his legs well supported; then apply the poultice, and moisten it with old sheep's butter; and heat it moderately at the fire, so that he can bear it; after which empty the turban from the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with another good treatment, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if you see cauterize him by making points many times over all the cauterizer.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing dries out the brain slowly; and then put cotton wet with vinegar in butter and with cow's fat.
de l’awe des eulz	with the eyes closed
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes to the eyes first as signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient this purifying thing for the head, and guard against all moisture, and make him sweat or bath many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that he orders to rub his head, and makes him sweat or bath many times while fasting. After this he does the cauterization on the head, and does two cauterizations on the temples so that they are dry together, each one next to the other; and guard against the blood coming out of the vein, and if you see too much blood flowing, then stop it with a cloth so that it does not flow.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision of cauterizing how you shall stop it; and never is cauterization done or hatred by cutting away the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	The two hearts of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and lie on the veins, or draw the arteries that are in appearance at the top of the head; and one can see that it is of cold, phlegmatic superfluity, then do the cauterization that I have said at the beginning of the awed descending to the tears: I cauterize the top, and two cauterizes on the two temples, and two cauterizes where they cut away the two bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes it well above the ear with all small cauterizes.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The hearts of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you use the medicines according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then done so much that he drinks three times with the medicine of the sick; after him he takes the head, and makes cauterization at his middle with olive cautery; and makes two cauterizations of the cautery called "clavis" on the two sorrows, a little more than the hair; and guard yourself from the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called "clavis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	from this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you make two cauterizations on the two sorrows as long as the sorrows are; and do not let your hand rest until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	hair that points to the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has come when the hair of the oils are converted to the parakeet, and touch the oil, and it is done on two ways: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and equal, then place the patient in your care; afterwards, sign on paper a figure that is also like the fur of the mirth, and is the beginning of the signature of the hairs; then put cotton soaked in wax and muskelloge of persillion on the oil, then heat the cautery so that this is the shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the affected area little by little several times, so that the scar is burned there; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up to the point where the oil is; then put your hand down, and leave it like this for III days, and then put cotton soaked in water in a poultice until the scorching is removed; after treating with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hair comes back, and the paper is softened then start again the fire on that middle point as you did first; and if the hair are gone, then cauterize until the paper is returned to its natural position, and is even, and does not touch the hair the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal fire cautery is that you command the patient to leave the hairs grow long and even, then make of parchment the shape of the bay leaf; then take of French soap and hot water, of each a .Z., and grind them well together; and do it quickly, so that it does not cool down, then in spreading on the shape that you made like the bay leaf leaf, put on the paper eyes; and if the illness is only in one oil spot, then must be applied in I too, and also in both feet; and moisten with cotton soaked in water in a box of ointment; and the patient's chiés should be in your hand and place your palm on the medicine, and press it little by little every time that the patient feels tingling from the medicine, for he feels tingling too like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	As you have had this for a long time, take this medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the medication is no longer necessary, then remove the bandage from the wound, and inspect it to see if the skin has healed as if it had been lifted by fire or cut; and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then continue to apply medicine to the wound as long as your cuts are still open and your hair is not yet grown in; then put cotton wetted with linseed oil on it until the scar tissue has healed, which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is well.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to, then wrap your wound carefully so that the medicine does not get on the hair.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft and the hair sticks into the oil, then start again with the medicine on the same spot that was softened by the paper, in the same way as you did before; after treating it, until it is well; and this is the form of the wound of the palm:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to what they can see; and do not give a straight answer to the one for whom the study of this art is required.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure for a fistula by caustic
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you perform a caustic cure according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dip cotton wicks in wine or cranberry juice on oil; then heat the caustic substance; and apply it to the scalp as if it were the form of a dove's feather; together, let the hair be burned from one side of the head to the other, and let it hang down like a tent, but nevertheless, let it burn well for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula is opened, and treated with poultices, and dried; and if it is closed, then treat it forcefully, and after put the hot cauldron firmly on, and hold your hand to the cauldron at the part of the nape behind the oil, that your hands do not go wild; and put the cauldron into the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the cauterization just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then restart the cauterization once more, and if you need to do it again, leave it for III days; after put cotton soaked in butter on it, and cure with desiccating medicine until it is healthy, and if forty days have passed and it is still not healthy, then put medicine that corrodes onto the bone; and treat according to what came out in the chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a way to cauterize a fistula, which no one of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Hear me out on a technique for cauterizing a fistula, something none of the ancient physicians have spoken of. Let's begin by identifying the location and then introducing a thin instrument to shape it properly:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And let there be the quantity of one .Z. of vinegar; and hold your hand firmly, so that the patient does not move at all, lest the vinegar corrode its oil; and it is right that you put cotton wadding wet with vinegar over the wound or bandage it: thus the vinegar will artfully find the site of the fistula, and cure it with a marvelous remedy.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula has been cured by the cauterization we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then let him administer the pustule to the nose, and bring the fistula to the root of the nose according to that which is appropriate in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	the furrows in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	For many times, furrows form in the lips, which are called "hair", and sometimes also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these furrows as we have described in the divisions, and the cure does not improve, then use a small surgical scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it carefully in the furrows as long as it comes out clean; after treatment, apply the balm of cerote until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after having made a poultice and covered it and it has become soft and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have described in the divisions, but it does not improve: then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after having sealed or pierced the fistula, and keeping your hand there until the iron comes out at its base, and doing so once or twice, after treating as we have described in the treatment, as long as it is healthy; and if it is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to discover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the pain of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are swollen with moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines, then put the head of the sick person in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its form comes out there in a certain way that you put a cord on the tooth; and place the cautery inside with great heat, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; then let go of your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; then fill the mouth of the patient with salt water, and leave it for an hour and rinse it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this manner, the tooth that was moving is set in place, and the gums that were swollen and sore are relieved and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the tooth pain comes from cold, or when there is frost, and the medicines do not help, then one must use two kinds of cauterization: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter if it is such that you squeeze butter from a cow's teats, and the tip in a spoon of iron or gold; after taking cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent, and the moisture in butter made, and put on the tooth aching badly and hold for as long as it is cooled; and thus often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and you see if such wet wool and cotton in butter freezes, and put on the aching tooth, and put on an iron hot until the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Cautery with fire if it is such that you squeeze a iron or gold chain, and let it be thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, so that its shape comes out, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will become severe on the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then suck it up; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cauldron out of the skull that you want, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the cauldron:
des scrophules	of scourges
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of cold moisture and do not submit to digestion with medicines, then heat the head-cauldron so that after comes the form, and has II openings for the fumes to rise to the cauldron on the other side; and put the cauldron hot on the abscess once, or where it is needed, as long as it comes to the root of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so for III days; and put cotton wet with butter as far as the burning is over; then cure with oil and camphor as long as he is well.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures triumph over the nostrils and most especially when it comes from a cold complexions, then the patient should be voided first by medicinal liquids; afterwards, cauterize at the root of the throat, and keep back from the nose but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, make another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let be the cauterization which is called 'clavicle' so that we have the form before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and disease of the nostrils are cold moistures, and the patient has no fever nor does he sweat, and the disease is old, then make him ij cauterizations on the nose in his holes; and another cauterization wet the pis between the breasts; and let be the cauterizations which are called 'clavicle' according to the form which is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make the cautery by piercing all the cautery that is called "poins" from which its shape is as described in the disease of the ears; and let the points be until XXX or more, where it turns around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Afterwards, treat the place according to what is said above, and let the cauterization be for three rainings according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for these where the cautery is lighter, for those where you make III together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, be gentle with the patient on his back and sides; afterwards, lift up what is inside the little finger of your left hand; and if the joint turns inwards, then heat the cautery that has two nails here according to this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound as far as the rib until it is scarred, and the shape of the cauterization comes with 4 cauterizations; and because it is done with the cautery that has 3 wires, because the shape of the cauterization is made with 4 cauterizes; and the nerve is according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the shape of the cautery that has 3 wires:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is applied on this nerve because there are 8 cauterizes.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards, put the fire on the flesh with a torch and let it rest, and do not move the member for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, what happens then? So make the cauterization on the thick part of the cautery with a nail, or with many cauterizes piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and the moisture is removed from the bones and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come coldness and moisture as long as it was extracted from its complexion, and there are many catarrhs to him, and to the usual methods of treatment he does not benefit, then the patient should be made to lie on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From then on, make three fire cauterizations in the anus of the back for the quantity of two coins, all three cauterizations are clamped, and two fire cauterizations on either side as long as the shape of the cauterization is at three angles, and there is a space between them that they are not joined together when they move; and let the cauterization be so perfect that it burns both parts, and the shape of the cauterization is according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see cauterized with a great fire according to this form; and the one who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by puncturing and signing on the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see from the head; then cauterize tothe whole fire which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment for the wound that we have had before, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, it comes pain from cold and moisture and strong windiness, as long as it is removed from its natural constitution by the excesses; and the patient is treated for what we have said in divisions, and it does him no good, unless the patient is gentle on his own bile; and mark the shape of three cauterizes according to this form and quantity on the liver, leaving a space between each cautery the thickness of two fingers; and let the cautery be as long as the length of the trunk, and do not press too hard all the way down the cautery; and let it be burned with such heat that the half of the cautery is blackened, and let the patient lie on his side; and if he cannot, then let him stretch out his legs, and raise his breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is, then cauterize these cauterices of the cutlet, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the meat, for you would make the whole body parched; and let it come to a single eye, for the cure is very subtle in place, and the sauces so that one can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you must know whether it is in the parenchyma of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the parenchyma, then feel the patient's pain is not too great; but if it is in the capsule, then feel the pain is very intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then, when this cure has ended the boils, the patient must be made to sneeze on his head; and then sign from above where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterizer that is similar to a blade, from which there is form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I cauterize as long as the burn is hot, and comes only to seeping, until the scar is all healed; after the cure according to the cure of leeches as long as it is healthy; and it does not come to this cautery but only those who have studied medicine for a long time, and by whom these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may courageously act, and I think that it is better to let it be.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	For the pleurisy cautery: The old ones said that one must make a cauterization for pleurisy with root of arhatology, and in this way: Take a root of arhatology long, the longest you can find, dry it, and also make it as thick and as long as your two hands; and wet it with oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize between the nipple and the neck, and II small cauterizations a little lower down on the side that is sore; and cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining it a little behind; and I cauterize under the breast, and another one above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and another one at the back of the shoulder from the previous one; and do not press your hand, but make it open as when you smell something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no old man used fire cautery resembling a razor, and sweeping it and placing it between the ribs until it comes to the aposteme; and he jumps out of pain, as we have said in the aposteme of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work is fear or the patient dies now, or fistula comes who cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
