When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they have three types of fire cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one way is that you do three cauterizations, or four, lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the fire cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, so that the patient shivers on his back; and another way of cauterizing is that you sweep the cautery which has two ners, as we have demonstrated in the dislocation of the shoulder; and put the scald which is at the place of the mouse, or the cuts of the mouse come toward the left side, and let the elevatations which you scald according to the scald, according to the length of the torso, and the cautery be according to the width of the torso.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the two nails have been burned for as long as the sound can be heard from the other side, then firmly apply the cautery, and in doing so you will have four. And if you see it, cauterize all of it with three.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure has been kept wet for a long time, and this is what must be done before the other one mentioned above.
de ydropisie	droopy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery does not work for droopiness, except in the manner called "ascleotes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the ways we have said in the divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations around the wound, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the kidney, and two behind the back along the spine, and one place under the pelvis. And let the cauterization be close to the skin of the cure.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leave the fire cautery to go the long time corruption, and do not let the cure of the sick after the cautery; and the recovery would be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the fire cautery for the abdomen is the clove that we have before us; and this for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is described here.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the skin
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the skin is swollen on the person who is dysenteric and is yellow in color, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the index and middle fingers; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, lest the yellow color be turned away, and the cautery is made according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After the fire cautery, make two cauterizations on each leg up to the toenail; and let one cauterization be long, one before the kneecap and one behind, between the legs; and leave the cauterizations above for a long time without treating them, because they will come off by themselves; after that, treat the other leg with the other treatments we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the house
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the stomach solution comes from cold and moisture, as long as the digestive and healing virtues that are in the stomach and in the small intestine remain intact, and cannot be cured by any remedies; and you will see the patient suffer greatly and have great strength, so do a great cautery on the stomach according to what he has spoken of before or a cautery of the stomach, a circlet; and four cauterizations around the anus carefully, one cautery under the testicles.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, make cauterization on his knuckles, and I cauterize each finger, and II small cauterizations on the stomach tenderly the great, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or one or more, and are old and have large cold and moist pus, and are cured as we said in the divisions, and it does not benefit, then do cauterizations: III on the spine of the back, that which is all further away from the spine almecdate little by little and in triangulating, and I cauterize away the two bones; and if you think that his stomach is cold, and the meat does not cook, and one sees swelling on the face, then the face has a great cauterization on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse at all cauterize clave; and leave the cauterization open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, let the wound heal until it is well.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnage that is called "thelulum
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you begin to cut the carnage (the tissue), if it is hot, warm the cauldron and then dip it into the carnage that has been cut; and leave it until the wound has healed, from which there is no pain; do this once or twice, and if there is any carnage left, cauterize it as we have said; after the beneficial remedies, take care that they heal until they are well; and if you cauterize with a large cauldron on the flesh, it will be more helpful.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound that has not been treated properly
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear a wound that is torn or opened, which we will describe in its place, if there comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	If there is no blood flow, and it is inflamed and covered with pus and corruption, then you must prove it with the entire subtle tent, and be careful that you know exactly how much of it is perfect.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery which seems like a razor, and pouring it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and restarting the cautery as many times as the corrupted and inflamed part is burned, one or three times according to the quantity of the needed treatment; and beware of the large veins which are involved, and the openings of the nerves.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula runs into the belly and intestine, beware of these veins, and do not make an incision except in the flesh, and believe that it is not persistent; after healing that part as long as it is healthy, and if the matter is dried up, know that the part is completely healed; and if the matter is not dried up, know that the part is three times corrupted, and the bone is rotted at the root; and thus as one of these things which we will explain in their places.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of the kidneys comes with great wind and does not respond to the treatment of women, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys from one side to the other at the clavicle cautery which we have just mentioned; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in line, and greater aid will be done.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from pain and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you make a cautery in the back part of the bladder, where the hair of the penis comes into contact with it, and one on each side, and each as long as a fingernail; and you make another cautery behind, where there is need; and you make the cauterization clavicle according to the shape mentioned above.
de la marris	from the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare is cold and moist, and does not allow itself to be conceived, and the flowers are corrupted and delayed in their term; and when they come, so they feel great pain: then it is necessary that he make three cauters around the bud, as we have said in the cauter of the bladder, and two cauters behind the back; and let the cauters be pegged, as we have said.
de la hainche	When the haunch is cold and moist, and does not allow itself to be conceived, and the flowers are corrupted and delayed in their term; and when they come, so they feel great pain: then it is necessary that he make three cauters around the bud, as we have said in the cauter of the bladder, and two cauters behind the back; and let the cauters be pegged, as we have said.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip bone-socket, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is farther away than the other when they are measured together; and the joints are found to be loose in the department, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the hip bone-socket at I cauterize resembling a circle, and sign before the joint around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and if it is, let the cauters be such as those with which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you don't have this fire cautery, make three cauterizations with the olive oil, and let the cauterizations be perfect like all the rest; and heal until he is well.
de la dolor de la hainche	for pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient with large pills of foul-smelling pills, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards, make the cauterization; and the method of the cauterization is according to two methods: that is to say, together with fiery medicines, and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is according to many methods, of which one is: that you cauterize on top of the hip three triangular cauterizations according to this shape, and make it deep and wide, and there between each cauterization leave a space the size of two, and let the olive oil cauterization; never do a cauterization in the middle on top of the head of the hip, for there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, whether the cautery is made with a ring that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains all the hip, and all the flesh of the kneecap is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is how it is done in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach up to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain comes up to the thigh and leg, then two cauterizations are made below where the patient feels the pain, and one cauterization above the ankle three times; either as a knife-cut cauterization or burning the flesh of the shin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or three on the foot or near the arch, then cauterize at those two or three places on the foot called "toes".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if his craft is, let him do it more; and if he feels that the pain is from the knee to the thigh, let him make a fire cautery with a knife or a circle, and you give him good guard in all your cauteries so that he does not leave them out as much as the cautery burns the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who made a fire cautery on the heel of the foot, and left them so much that the leg was all wrinkled, and the bones too, and it was pierced and corrupted all the bones.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a remedy for the belly that killed him.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if his pain is in two parts together, make fire cautery in one and the other, according to this way.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sage said in the cautery of the hip, from which this is the way, make one iron big and thick as an onion peapod, or a little less, and space between them the quantity of a pea pod; and let the intertrunks be on both sides, and also like peas, and I have many well-made irons; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is completely red and hot, and then put it on the boot of the sore leg, and let it turn round the back of the thigh; and let it be cauterized once more, and leave it for three days; and then make a poultice of butter, and leave the open wound long; after the cure of the injury until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Buqaqum says that we should use little of this cautery because of the danger of scalds, and few people use it; but this is a good cautery, which can bear it, and let him where it burns.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medical cautery of burning should be made like this: between the margin of the wound and a wall or a panel of wood, with a height of two hands, and with a thickness of two inches; it should be opened from side to side, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put on the chest of the horse, let the patient lie on his back next to his side; and put your hand much above on the chest of the horse; after get between the two circles of hot awl that are heated in the fire a poc, and leave it an hour ten, and suffer the patient the heat and pain.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it will prove the same as fire; and when the medication has passed, remove your hand with the instrument and raise the horse's leg of soft awl, and leave it for three days, and put on wax as much as the black scorching is healed; and let him rest for three days until it heals; and that one who follows behind will help after the cure of ointments as long as he is well.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends only to the thigh or only to the leg, make the awl burn according to what you have done in the hainche gradually; and this is the way of hot awl, and I have written it where the medicine is rectifiered.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Get alkali and live chalk, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together and put them in a nine-pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Take some small slots in which the tip of a risc can enter; and place that pot on top of another pot that is well sealed, and pour alkali and live chalk and sweet water into it, so much as to cover the two powders with it; and leave it like this until it has passed through it twice with water and see where the pot is sealed; then take all the water out and pour it over the chalk and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then if it is well water and is amenable to the work of medicine and other cauterizations; Because it performs such a work as fire, and if it has other medicines, all of which are mixed together with soap, all of these things.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galliens tells us of a remedy where one man was cured of the pain in his thigh and sciatic nerve, and he had great heat, and he said that no other remedy was made, and that he was healed on one soul when this cure was done, and he bathed himself as it is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he said in this way that you squeeze the green and fresh chalkstone well and dry it, and grind it with a little fat, and put it on the thigh and the leg and the hip where the pain is, and leave it; and let it be for III hours and because of the quantity so that the sick person does not feel the burning anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then he makes him enter or bath until his body is a little bit heated, and he makes him enter the bed, and the pain will go away all of it and will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medicine unless after the evacuation of scar tissue.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyscolores says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a goat's horn, it helps a lot; and the cautery must be done in some way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another and burn it with oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb and the other one called phalange.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After take a goat's horn dry, and hold it in the fire until it is coals, and lay it on the wool, and leave it until it is cold; and do this again, and never stop doing this as long as you think that it comes to the hip, and the pain stops; and this way of cauterizing is called "goat' horn cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of two pains
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or by sitting down or by impact or by too much evacuation, or by the appearance of expanded cold matter, there is no remedy for these appearances except that those who come from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that the patient voids himself of foul pills or other appearances, that one make on his back where the pain is, three lines signed with a cross, and in each line V cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cauterization be made according to the cauterization called 'pin'; and if you see, make III cauterizations or IV according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Often this disease comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have constricted spine when they stand up and fear; and you find in the back upper spine and the appearance that comes on the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this person and you treat him, if you cauterize with fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cauterizes each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize inside the spine with a fire that is two or three lines long, and let the wounds be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After you have treated the area until it is healthy according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply fire in places where there are nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When there is pain in the joints due to moisture that spreads to each limb, and when pain occurs in parts, what is called "podagra" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicines, then it is cured with fire in this way: make the fire cauterize around the joint of the foot, and let the fire be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you grasp on the face of the foot, then perform cauterization with all the cauterizations that are claimed to be "none".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the genitals and to other joints, and this happens many times, then perform cauterization on each knee with three cauterizations or four of each part, with olive cauterization; and if you need more, then do more, but only hold your hand firm for as long as the flesh of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains come down to the genitals and to the back, then administer the cauterization that we have spoken about in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then perform a pinch of the fire twice; and if there is still pain in the two joints of the fingers, then perform a pinch on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and govern the patient well and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do this good governance, and you purge phlegm, then will you be healed by God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syrup
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in anger, and the balls descend into the bowels and it is newly, then it is that when you see him cured, he does not vomit any more that day; and he uses things that make his belly light, so that the end descends from his belly; after he sits down on his back between your hands, and he orders him to wash his hair as long as the balls are repaired, and he takes them with your hands, and signs an inch above the rupture on the bone of the hand, and there is a sign that is like half a circle over the heart; then heat the fire
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it drops senteles.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then return the balls to their place; and let the minister dry his hand so that it does not turn back; and work well the legs of the sick person, and put a cuff on him I and I serjant on the legs, and another one on his foot which dries his hands; then put the fire cautery on your sign all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you touch the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, then start again another time until you reach the bone; and take care carefully that the ball does not slip when you make the cautery; that you do not burn him; and so that by this fire the sick person does not die, or another bad.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you come up to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the fire cautery of children be subtle according to their measure, and of adults also great according to their measure; after III days cure his place of the cautery of butter until the warming is done; after the cure other oilings until he is well, and lay the sick person on his back for XL days until the wound is well fixed; and it is necessary that his medications be taken long enough, so that the ball does not slide when he prays to go to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, a well-made bandage is brought to him and kept for another forty days; and good rest, that he work little and beware of too much drinking and eating, and too loud shouting; and when he has done this teaching, let him be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here the cure of cutting in his ointment.
de la routure dou ventre	of a rupture from the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, do the cautery of cautery according to its quantity, and let him have third of the cure; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancient ones said that one should cauterize at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is the place of the incision and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another further back, and all your hand around all the cauterized place.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is gentler and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any member, or from a sprain or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the cure with medicine does not help, then it is appropriate that he be cauterized at the fire which is called "poins", and the cauterization is according to the length of the member and its smallness and its feebleness and its virtue and its location from torments and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is well after the first cauterization, it is good; but if not, begin another cauterization on top of that one, for the custom is that fire must be applied to the member that is nearest to him so that you should make the cauterizations as long as the patient remains ill.
de meselerie	of confusion
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The pains are helped by no heat but much aid, and most of the disease comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Do not see the cautery, but beware that the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division of diseases, and does not cause pain or delay, and you doubt that corruption will permeate the whole malady, then make five cauterizations on the top of the head: I cut off the hair from the top, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; and one behind on the nape; and I leave it so that the cauterization comes to the bone, and so long as the scabs come out without it, so that the vapors of the heavy humors can come out; and the cauterize on the mouse according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if his digestion is scattered everywhere; and it loses manifestly, so that you must have the fire cauterized by these cauterizations that we have said at the beginning, and one cauterization in his neck, and two cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one great cauterization on the head and another deliciously, and two on the shoulders; and two on the kidneys, and two on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I make cauterizations, the more help it gives, and the more benefit it brings; and know that the patient feels no pain from the cauterization as the healthy person does, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure, leave the face of flour with honey and other cures as long as it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling comes to any member and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healthy, then make the cauterization on the member according to its greatness and smallness; and let the cauterization be a little bit entered into the flesh of the cure; and then cure with ointments until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no time is done cauterization and by hand and at the foot and at the back, at the outlet of the nerve that silences the member, and so if it is osteized; and nevertheless it does not interfere with him unless he knows the members and outlets of the moving heart.
de albaras	of albars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albars" is awake, and the medicine has no effect, then cauterize with a perfect fire, according to the quantity of the remedy, until the blush is taken away, and its color changed; then cure with flour of beans and lentils with oil of roses and plantain leaves, and blood of cabbage and almond, each in part; and mix them all together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the affected area until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for leprosy by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the leper begins to appear, and you see it stop spreading, then cauterize with a fire that seems like a circle, surrounding the entire area of the leper.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet some say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the leper's wound; and yet I do not think this is good, because it might cause it to become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never heard of this being done with any success; and rather, it is better to cauterize all around, with the fire called "a circle", as we have said in many cases of cauterization.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the inflammation that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some people have a disease called "adubelati", and it takes a long time to die or because of the excess blood that it produces or because the patient is very old and has little blood, or because they are very young; then you will see them hurry to die: so cauterize them with small fire in piercing; then leave them like this.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you pierce her with all the cauterizing, let the fire of the cauterizing be hot:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterizing has pierced the blood, and let there be such cauterizes that the patient feels cold in some way so that the course of the pus is stopped.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure, as long as he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease, which is called "corrodens," is not anything other than a putrefaction of the member, for it mangles the members just as fire dries up the wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in its early stages, which can be treated with fire, then heat the claves carefully, small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the disease is; after cauterizing all sides, so that you completely remove the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that everything that is corrupted is taken away by osteid.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the burned members oil to soften them as much as the burnings of fire are healed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of the causes of pain with garlic.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days a scar does not heal, it is good; and if it does not, begin again the fire cautery on that which is delayed from its place corrupt.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this treatment is never cured with medicine for the fire cautery; but the fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said above concerning the treatment of the medicine for the wound; take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the onions that come to the edge
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Sometimes it happens that after cuts, a disease called "clots" forms according to our intention, and it is a large faulty thing that bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cautery of this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say Fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautery with fire so that you heat cautery as a feather of a vulture, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can poke the nail from all sides, and that it has subtle edges; after, place it hot on the nail, and wrap your hand completely around the nail until it comes out at the tip; and leave it like this for III days until it starts to move putridity; then make a poultice of wild marjoram crushed with vinegar, and leave the poultice on all night, and let the nails come out and will be rooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with a poultice of marjoram crushed with vinegar, and leave it on all night, and let the nails come out and will be rooted from their roots. And then cure the wound by covering it with soil until it heals.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the neck is twisted by defers, and many times comes and in hand and piez, it is necessary that you bring fire to it; and this is a little way: take a chain of iron or of metal, or a feather of a vulture, and put it on the nail and the althelma, that is to say, porrels warts; and put the chain on so that it turns red all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep path up to the root; and suffer the patient a little the stinging of the hot water an hour; then let him be, and he will be rooted from all his roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Ensi fai an aprés autr, tuntu esrai chi tuzu cös si ston kors, pui li kuri de oignimenz ki engenan chér.
li cure dou trembler	Thus, make another preparation, while you burn all those who are in the core, then cure the odor that causes fever. The cure for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake from cold, or from quartan fever or other, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizations on the spine of the back, a cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization at the feet, and one above the stomach with olive oil cauterizing; this will stop the shaking, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No times do appear on the body by sweating, or pustules that come from corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is the first time that they appear, then you must make a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a delicate cauterization with oak gorse, so that the tip is taken from fire, or with the root of aristeology at a distance, or with the lenticular cauterizer.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And in no way are the cauterizations done at the beginning when it begins, according to this method, and they cannot grow hair before, but the excess is broken off, and they are cured; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are often great pains of blood from the artery that is cut to the wound, which comes to the surface, or to incising an abscess, or to cauterizing a member, and similar things; it is a most terrible thing to stop bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And in any case, when you have one, if you are in a hurry to put your index finger on the wound of a vein, and draw it out little by little until your blood stops flowing from the hole that it has made, and then put fire to olive oil, small or large, as much as it is red; then take I, or a great or a small one according to the wound and its place, and hold the cauterizer on this vein where you are holding your finger, and keep the cauterizer in place until the blood stops flowing.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if you pricked when you lay your two fingers above a vein, and the cauterization has stopped, then take another of the cauterizations that are in the fire quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other as long as the blood is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is delicate, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when the artery is cut short of the vein, it cannot be stopped well anyway unless by one of the four ways we have said: or with cauterization, or with extraction if it has not yet been treated, or with a strong thread tied, or with medicines put on which have the power to stop the blood; and let it be bound and stretched carefully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer a strict binding with cloth or place burning things on it, or similar things, if it does not help, then do not do it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Et s'il n'a pas de miroir ni de remède à portée de main, alors il doit placer son index sur la plaie de la veine comme nous l'avons dit, et bien étirer jusqu'à ce qu'il se soit arrêté sur la plaie et la veine; et ne le remuer que s'il est humide d'eau froide souvent car il faut que l'eau soit froide autant que possible jusqu'à ce que le sang soit gelé et épaissi et arrêté; et faire des enfoncements avant celui à qui il faut faire des cautères et des médicaments.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have spoken to you in the first chapter about all diseases in which fire cautery, or burning medicine, and squirts, causes and instruments, and the shapes of cauterizations are needed; and I put this chapter from the top to the bottom, and I will go in this chapter through the middle way for those who suffer more lightly than those who want it.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I have begun to speak of this, it is necessary that you learn that with this ointment there is more danger and fear than with the first cautery, and for that reason more caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not take any foolish actions.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in the ways of people come to cure.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who because of their disease have died easily due to the foolishness that results from their illness, and from the great severity of their disease, then we should be afraid of them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these things which you have told me, and said: "Wait, I am getting better"; and the disease is mockery.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not right that you should consent to these people who come to you with this manner of speech, but rather place greater confidence in your honor than in your own desire, and do not open widely but carefully from the one of whom you are certain, and from whom you might have taken and lost; and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your patients that health may be converted; and he who will help you to gain a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and may you wish for the divine inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in devising by chapters, according to that which is before or fire cautery, which I have devised from the beginning up to the end, for you to find more easily that of which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dou chief plein d’aigue
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Now this child is often afflicted with this disease, and when the baby cries too much the head of the child is restrained too tightly; and it is never said that this is the cause, so let us not say it again.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur except in children, and all those whom I have seen it affect have died; and for this reason I believe that we should be more cautious in the treatment of this disease.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose neck was swollen with fluid, and whose head became heavy until it could not be held up; and because of the moisture it seemed that he would die, and this moisture gathered around the spine between the cheek and the bone; and the head, because of this moisture, is swollen and the abscesses are small, so cut a large slit in the head, as far back as possible; and also observe the shape of the spinal column:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is thicker, and the abscess is larger, so make two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If the moisture is soured by the bone and you see the folds of the cheek opening from each side, and when you press it with your hand towards the inside, water does not come out and it does not return to its place: then you should make three incisions on one side of the cheek according to this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract the moisture all at once.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, remove the dressings and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that for five days; then take off the dressing, and treat the wound with ointments and oils, and let the head be dried up equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to incision is that you consider where the length of the abscess, and the assembly of the needle; for it is never before; never behind; never on the right; and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess length is, and the needle assembly, and do it according to what you can; and beware that you do not seal the artery; and come away with blood, so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of healing
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is a disease called "cataract" or "pit", and the disease is old, and the medicine cure does not benefit, then the second cure is to make a cauterization with that which will seal the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, when you can see them seal, that the patient covers his head; after rubbing the place with an rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extract the patient's hair from all of it; then inspect where the veins enter, and their locations on either side of the ears, and they are raised; then sign the lines of the cheeks, then cut them both with a sharp scalpel, so that the sawing goes down to the bone, and this is done on both sides.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, close the mouth of the artery and tie the knot above, carving also as I have said across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, let the blood flow continually without ceasing.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the sense, then you must measure the quantity of the space of III inches, then sign with a needle and cut down to the bone; and what is needed to put blood out so it is VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone no room for bleeding, if the cut apotomies do not come, then draw the wound and bind, and the cure of the wound with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of shaving
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient toothache comes, and catarrh is acquired, because of the moisture of tears and fever in the temples and old sores and similar things, it is treated with medicines by the ways of medicine remedies and none of them benefit, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is that the patient makes his hair grow in his temples again, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens very well with its beating, and is not too tightly closed except in some people who are too cold; and if it is closed, then the patient removes his collar from some sheets, then he rubs the place with any harsh cloth, and raises the place of warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatumile where this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	puis escorche le cuir légèrement tant que tu viens à l'artère, puis la trais en haut comme pincées, et la dépare bien des toiles que sont désوز li de chescune partie; et s'il l'artère est sottilz, si la tourne à la pointe de l'uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantité des II chiés.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then scrape the skin lightly as you come to the artery, then trais it up like pinches, and pare well the webs that are desoz li de chescune partie; and if the artery is sottilz, so turn it to the point of the uncine, then cope that part according to the quantity of II chiés. For if it is not copped, the sans would not be all in all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And trais dou sanc of VI c/ to III; and if the artery is grans, so it is necessary that you tie it in II leus of a double strong thread of silk, which porriture does not i come before the suddenness of the wound, and come decorremens of sanc; then cope the superfluity that is between the II lines at that hour meisme, and then, if you see, so cauterize with the cautery cutellaire jusc’a l’os as long as the chiés are copped; and this is the muedre oevre, if the malaides does not have fievre and he is of a chaude complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is an aid to end moisture; for this is a more great aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the artery with fine cotton and place it on well-made tentures; and when you remove them, use dry medicines that cause the formation of charcoal and tentures, as long as they are healthy; and if without a stop from the artery you cut so much as you can, quickly cover it with cauterization, or employ vitriol on it and strain it in your hand until the clot is hardened; and if you do not have this present, place your finger in cold water for as long as the clot hardens, and remove it as much as it comes off; and that which is wetter and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting from two sides, but let the cutting be well-spaced so that it lasts longer on fire.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too soft, then it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two knives a line of space, and then when you have signed off the two legs, and you put on there the fiery iron as long as it comes up to the bone, and cut the vein in two lines; and be distant between the two shoulders because he is not stuck to this fire instrument from all sides; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes come out of the veins that are on the top of the head of the shoulder, and there is no benefit from the medicine that I make, and you see the face of the patient turn black, and feel a feverish sensation as if it were cold; and if the oil is soft and moist so that the hair of the eyelids falls, and the eyelids are burnt by the heat of the tears, and they are scorched by the fire of the tears, then there is need for this cure.
