des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the fingers cause a hard, grainy-looking abscess to form in each lip; then you should cut each one open and pick out the contents with tweezers, and apply vitriolic brooches to each one according to their size, until the sore is healed; and then let it air out, and treat the dry parts until they are well.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the tooth root causes a swollen gum that the old people call "albulus"; if it is necessary, you hold it with tweezers and cut off the tip at its root, and then apply vitriolic brooches or other binding and drying powders; and if this swelling comes back after the incision, and many times it does, if you cover it again, and cauterize it: if it does not come back after cauterization, and this is the way to cover it.
des sordens	of the orders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	of the orders
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from pain that you wait to draw out as much as you can, because there should be no excuse for not drawing it out. For this substance is very high until then such that one cannot find an excuse for not drawing it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	So when the patient is painful to be drawn, then you must be sure of the teeth that grind.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the patient is gone, and he believes that his tooth is good, and makes him grind the good tooth; however, this does not relieve the pain until he is drawn out, for we have already tried to do this with these elders; and when you are sure of the grinding tooth, so it is worth you scratch the tooth at all with a sharp file; then let him move your two or small pliers on the first hole and hole as much as it is well loosened, then he securely locks the pliers; and let the head of the patient in your lap, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is correctly extracted without breaking it, and if it does not move anymore, then take any of these instruments and pour it inside each part lightly, and shake it so as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if his jaw is tight and swollen, you should fill it with tow, where the gaps are; and if he is held gently with pliers so that it does not break when pulled out; and it is necessary to clean thoroughly around the gums to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And do not break it, and there remains a part of it, and returns to the patient by the mischief of the root, causing greater pain than the first one did.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself from doing this in the same way as that foolish surgeon does, who often breaks the jaw by his haste and audacity, and never does what we have described; but he brings it about sometimes by the burning of that great disease for the roots, or by the breaking of the jaw, as we have often seen; and when the jaw is drawn out, if you wash the place with wine or aqua vitriolis and twine, and take care not to draw it out suddenly, so that it may not come about that often happens, that it often comes about, if you employ the place of vitriol. And if this does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that they do not mute the teeth first, are long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of strong members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and have teeth to hold them in place.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root moves when pulling, it is necessary to put cotton damp with oil or butter in the hole.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the roots are soft, for then the pliers called 'algefri' are inserted, which makes the jaw look like a beak; and be inside made as a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then it is necessary to uncover the whole tooth around the root, and place the instrument called 'althali', that is to say a file, this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be large and strong so that it does not break, and the root jumps out because of it, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the tools, from which the forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help yourself with this instrument that has two heads, from which this form comes:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front of the density of the teeth, and this instrument that seems a pair of large pliers, from which this form comes:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is good that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not worth counting; and the master subtil chooses his own instrument according to what his work and the disease demonstrate to him, because there are many diseases where the old teacher does not teach an instrument for the diversity of them; and if it does not break the carriage or other bones, on which it will lie, if he seeks the instruments that are appropriate to it, I have told you, and helps himself with gestures, from which this form comes:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-fitting to hold the bone in place, so that it does not escape but can be held and cut off; and then return it to its proper place with medicine suited for this, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, so make a hole with all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not seem to fit the natural shape of the jaw, and their form is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you know whether the roots are inside after the tooth, and they are not in their right place, and cannot be sewn or filed: then file; and if it is rooted with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape I will show you, which is like a small claw, and is made of iron, made in one piece:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits and fits tight to the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then file with a sharp file like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the lime where we make needles; and in lime the tooth pokes and pokes in the hands gently every day so that it does not move until it chokes; then the plane at the end to any razor, and the dense is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to grind the sharpness as long as it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the teeth loosen, either by percussion or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on what he chews without choking, and you have cured them with restrictory medicines, and that does not work; if you are to restrain it with a gold wire, because silver wire becomes green and rusts, but gold wire never moves; and make sure the wire is neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you notice any gaps between the teeth, take the wire and wrap it double between two healthy teeth, then place the chiés between the teeth, if there are one or more, until you have cleanly covered up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start to cover again up to the part where you started, and tighten your hand gently and carefully until it no longer moves; and make sure that your ligature is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the heads of the wires to a set of pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth and place them so that they do not damage the tongue; and then leave them as tight as possible, and if they fall out or the wire comes off, tighten it with another wire; if it is delayed and will serve thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the attachment of the healthy II teeth and the II molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then, when the tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not skilled and patient should do this, and never make the shape of a tooth of an oak, and put it back in its place where it fell out, and tighten it as we have said, and delay and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	for a cold
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	for a cold
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	and if the fever comes on, then put vinegar on the burn; and if it doesn't go away, then cauterize it with the caustic, which is good for that; then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see a red or black or hard spot that the patient doesn't feel or touch, because it is a boil; and if it is turning yellow and there is moisture, then pour the caustic, and make a fine fent with a sharp razor, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if he is not better after your treatment, then put vinegar on it broiling until it has scarred, and then return to your treatment until you have done all; then lift up the leech of air and salt, and treat him with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	of the throat abscesses which are called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they do not heal, take care: if it is a hard abscess of little size and white color, don't touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is thick, don't touch it with iron either for fear of bleeding; but let it rest until it has cooled down, and then remove it, for it might burst by itself; and if it is a white color, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see that the abscess is cool and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders be well supported, and he opens the mouth and puts his fingers between his teeth, and presses the tongue against all the instrument, so that it takes shape; and it should be silver or gold as fine as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And see the anus, then take the knife and put it into the anus, and go up further than you can; and don't put anything in with it, but rather wrap the instrument in a cloth, so that it looks like a bunch of wires; and yet the head is bent, and one side above the other, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or some other metal.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument, take a cloth and tie it like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be careful not to cut too deep on one side or the other; and when you have wrapped one of the anuses, do the same with the other according to this same way, and afterwards gargle the patient with hot water, and do it often, and let him not get sick, if he gurgles with water cooked apples or leaves of mirthe, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then care for him until he is well; and never cut other abscesses in the throat than the two anuses, if you cut them carefully as those.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I had a woman with an abscess in her throat, which was small; and I closed the whole throat very tightly so that the woman could not breathe through the canal which was constricted, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like this for one more day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had risen twice its size through the two openings from which it had emerged.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	So I hastened, and inserted a hook in one of the openings, then lifted it high, and pulled hard, and extracted a long piece of bow; then refitted another hook in the other opening from which it had emerged, and pressed her tongue; then I inserted the hook into the abscess, and filled some of it, and there came out only a little drop of blood; so the canal in the woman's throat was completely blocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting the abscess for a long time; and the abscess receded, and filled the space that I had previously emptied, until it grew very large again; so I tied it up and cauterized it inside her throat: so it stopped growing; and I left those parts behind, and God did the rest afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the rectum comes out of its place and is far away, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is big and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the abscess is soft, and thin, so you should cut it; and that which is round and assembled and is not far away; and it is bloody or of pale color or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, of its blink and its distance, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue on the instrument which we have mentioned above; then insert the awl into the eye, and twist it, and cut with the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; because if you cover more, it will grieve the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two testicles, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use fire cautery on the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in your lap, and then press the tongue of the instrument that we have said or fire cautery onto it, and conflagrate with sharp fire, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using this instrument's motion, from which this form comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be a hair or thread where the medicine is put, as if it were a spoonful of medicine, and hold the instrument to all the medicine on the uvula; and let the patient lie gazing on his back, so that saliva and spittle run out of his mouth from the medicine, lest it go down his throat, and burn him; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it onto the uvula, the quantity of a half hour, until you see it become dark and the medicine taste sweet; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton over the root, until the cotton dries; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after three or four days clean out what is inside of the medicine; and be arrosezed with cold water, and cure with gargles as long as he is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the incision, save for the cauterization. If it is cured with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and ysope and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all into a pot or some of them; and I put it there easily, and make it boil; and the pot shall be well covered with a lid, and the instrument chewed up according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	It shall be of silver or of gold, and let one of the shoulders be boiled in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises up the vein by the cannula, until the vein is dead; afterwards you may begin again frequently, until the vein dries out, and be careful not to make it hot at the beginning of the advent of an abscess, for many things can happen; and do not make it hot except at the decline of an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put a nail in the patient's mouth so that it does not get too hot; for the nail does not make the breath very hot, and this is good treatment together, healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Several times it rises in the throat, a bone or a fish, or nothing; so that you must take what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and if what is not opened up for you and is put back in the throat, it is good that you make the patient vomit in such a way that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if this thing is thrown up by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of bread dried up; and you tie the sponge to it, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, if it rises strongly, and then pull hard; and if it does not come up with what we have said, then take the instrument of pluck according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and has the head raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of it come off, nor does it push the bone in; and move it so that the patient swallows the instrument, for whatever it is moving or rustling; if it swallows it, or it draws it out evenly, as far as it can go.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine for this blood, as I said in the division, by means of medication; and when it does not benefit, then look at the patient's tongue to the sun, so that you press it against the instrument which I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, if you draw it out with a small hook, or with delicate hooks that are worth anything.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a dog's teeth, and put them in the throat of the sick person, then pour or blow on the dog's teeth until they burn, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is losing their hair all over their body every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in slowly, so that it doesn't choke, and move it into his hand often; and if soon as he feels the water, spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he doesn't spit as we have said, then smoke the sick person with ashafetida, using the instrument that I mentioned in the smoke treatment for the uvula; do this many times, because it won't cause a dry mouth.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of smoke treatment is as follows: you should squeeze the charcoal in a pot where it can fall into the middle, and put the instrument's tip in that place; then pour your smoking substance, and let the sick person put the end of the cane in their mouth and close their mouth, so that the smoke doesn' t come out, but goes directly to the uvula; and the uvula will start to burn now, and if it doesn' t spit, then start the treatment again many times; and make the patient thirsty, and give them salty things and ale, and don't let them drink water; and then the doctor should see what is happening with this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument appears as if it were claws bent for entering the throat; and has a resemblance to a hook, and is sharp like limestone so that whoever takes hold of it cannot let go; and see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the instruments of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Mouths of شبیهy to an abscess are, according to what the memory comes here before and after in this book, and they are diver en perforation et en taille; et c'est en II manieres dont l'une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu'il tient moistor.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is so that they are for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess at the head is different from that at the base, and the abscess at the charnuted part is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses it is not necessary to pierce, as long as the bowels are dying according to their completion; and if to such that it is necessary to pierce when they are cured, and do not die according to their completion, as to an abscess that are delicate joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from delicate joints, and it is left as long as it is putrefied inside, for fear that the ligature and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contracture in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is from the principal limb, and you delay the perforation as long as it is putrefied, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is from the foundation, if you pierce it thus while it is cured without digestion complete, so that the one which is from the foundation does not putrefy completely, and be stretched inwards, and comes to a fistula; and cannot heal thoroughly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforating the abscess which is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the argument and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make sit the perforation where it depends most on the abscess, and at the place where it opens; and let the perforation be long of the body, and the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and in the nigh parts and in the arteries, and in all its even parts where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, by that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in the charnute place, if it moves so that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce him in front, if you draw out his blood from within, and it is full of dirty water; and perhaps his lips become hard and his breath becomes difficult.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limbs require.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should bring small abscesses to a head, small pustules, and with large abscesses, large pustules, and many splits according to the appearance of their size; and if there are such abscesses that have come to a head and have healed over, so that they look like patches of skin, and if they are large, so that they are torn open again; and if there are such abscesses that are split into three angles, and if there are such that are split in half, as with an abscess on the back; and if there are such that are split lengthwise, and other shapes that seem to have been cut.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the hopes of treachery do not ever jump with the issue of the bow, lest the patient die, and you don't notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this medicine with great care, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is small, then apply a linen or old cotton bandage; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, then tie each one so that they come together; and if you have wrapped part of the skin in a cloth, and have sewed it up, then fill it with dry cotton or a drenched linseed poultice, and leave it like that for three days; then open it up, and treat the bone with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood from the wound runs into your face, then bring cold water and rinse it quickly, and moisten the cloth, and put it on the running place again and again.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood from the wound persists, then bring a remedy and treatment, and the powders that I have said to hand in this book, and if it is a wound of the nose or mouth, and the aposteme or the hole is very nervous, then know that you should put on top bedsheets and drapes soaked with wine and oil and warm; and if it is gangrenous, and the leg is fleshy, then know that you should soak the drapes in water and oil or cold wine for three days, as we have said; and then clean out the aposteme and wash it and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is known everywhere in the treatment of abscesses: however I told you before how one should go about treating abscesses, and here is the ointment.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	How to treat small sores, and they are handled by us in the manner of a net, also like the joint of a tree, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fat and soft ones where there is moisture as well as dry ones; and some are hard and bony at the edge, and there is no doubt that the artery does not work contrary to it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so that you experiment with all the instrument called "entremessoire", from which the form comes out later, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and this comes out by itself.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, if it shrivels up nothing leaving the peel which contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when it is left nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; otherwise, in water and seel, and employ the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed by night.

Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds only a little fat, if the cup follows this form, long; and pour your oils, and peel off all, and put all your treatment to draw the meat away from the skin; and if the artery makes contrary, do what I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so you will do to the abscess if it is painful, and with the chisel and with the cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the painful abscess and on the wet one, for it is lighter, because there is little blood.

And if any of these abscesses or chisel or have no moisture, and the same kind of abscess that I hit with a chisel on the back of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a heavy stone, sharp and white, and couldn't break it; and if we had hit any of them, we would also have caused a wound as if it were a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come out of the cheeks, those that come from the children and from the roots of the ears, let the opening be all the way up to the most dependent place so that the bow can come out; and cure them as they should.
des scrophules	of the sores
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there comes an abscess to the throat, and it seeps, and it puts forth ulcers, and never comes to another place or to the cors, and are rotten, and are infected one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each sore is properly within its rib, as the nose and the abscess at the base of the skull, as we have said before; and the appearances of these sores are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in those that are of good disposition for the neck, and seem like the color of the flesh, and do not move from any part, nor is it deep; so you must cut it from above, and scrape each part, and these two lips of the mouth with one finger, if you need to, as we have said before in the case of an abscess at the base of the skull; and little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor is it too deep, so that the hand does not escape, and do not look too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol broach, or some powders that stop blood, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound has calmed, if you return to your work, as long as you do it; then feel with your index finger whether there are any small scars, if so, cut and clean them up.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a great vein at the root of the scrofula, it only comes that you cut this scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double knot, and let it hang by it, without doing any harm; then employ the wound with old cloth dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have gathered all the scrofula, then you must gather the two lips of the wound and sew them together immediately, so that there is no delay due to the abundance of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary for you to go to the root and draw it out strongly, and to sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce them so that they die; and pierce them in the same way as that which has been mentioned before, depending on it, then apply oil with care and similar things, so that they do not corrupt those who are delayed from corruption; and when the wound is well washed, then treat it with oil, applying it so that he may be healed.
de squinance	from scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones said and spoke about the swelling of the throat; but I have never seen it happen in our land, and it is the scriptural word of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit in the throat, which is called the epiglottis, be removed; and for this no help should be sought from anyone, since all the veins and the pharynx of the sick person are at the back of the mouth or throat or two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the throat channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so that the obstruction which comes from strangulation does not occur.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it with three or four small slits across the back, between two circles or by the amount of the slit in the flesh, not in the cartilage; and if this is possible for cutting the epiglottis so that there is no need for a knife, and the blade is long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece. des nous	of us

quant li boude ist fuer	How long should it be kept wet?

As the appearance of the boil comes out by fire cautery or by incision of a pimple, and is on the belly and there are some boils, so as it happens in other ruptures, or of blood that comes out of veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if it is by the rupture of the pimple and by the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and opening of different issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the issue of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when you press it to its two sides so that it turns, and then comes back, and perhaps if it is stuck, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath and by great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit. Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	And if it's due to moisture, it's a light thing, and you must open well when you press it in your hand, do not constrain it; and if it's because of blood, open by these signs the large and hard apothema, and fix it according to a quantity; and if it's because of wind that escapes, know that the opening is made at the touxier, and the openings are such that you look at the appearance, it's for the blood of the artery, or the vein, or the wind.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you before, for the abscesses, for the artery, and for the vein.

dou chancre	Dou chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	Double cancer: We have spoken in the division about the appearance of cancer, and how it should be operated on with medicine, and how it should be avoided to cure it with iron; and we say that cancer is inherited in the breast, and great caution must be taken in its treatment, and the old man says that when cancer is in place where it can be cut as cancer is in milk, and in the chest, and in similar places, it must all be cut off when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, it should not be approached, for I have never found one who has been cured of it; nor has anyone ever been cured of it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound that continues for a long time like other wounds; however, when we do this operation of our own will and especially on children, it is necessary to do it in the best way and in the lightest manner for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not mention circumcision for their children, since they did not use it in their laws; we have acquired this only through experience.
