And when he is swollen, heat him up with the third method: dip a sponge or a thin drape in warm water only, or cook it in squinant and cumin and spicery, and strain the intestines until the swelling comes out; and never do this while resting, and let it lie that it may be cured by itself.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go away, moisten the intestines with water or wine and dry herbs are cooked, for by this way the entrance is slightly closed to a few things; and if it cannot enter, then cut a little hole in the wound with the instrument where one cuts the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to lie down so that he does not move much, because we do not need to cut him unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: if you split it inside and turn it over, and look at it like this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines protrude, if you can return them to their natural place in their own proper place, for this is difficult.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large and is in the lower part of the abdomen, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if the wound is in the lower part of the abdomen, let the head and chest be raised higher than the lower parts; and in this way it is fitting to treat what I have said about large and painful wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, you should dress them, then take two needles and a strong thread; according to the size of the wound, cut off a piece of thread that is as long as the width of the wound, then leave two inches of space at either end, and insert the needle or needles from one side of the wound to the other, passing through both sides of the skin as if you were sewing a shirt; then take two pieces of thread, each half an inch long, and tie them together at one end, and pass them under the first stitch, so that they are well hidden; then sew the edges of the wound together with these threads, leaving about two inches between each stitch; this method is good for small wounds, but for larger ones you should use smaller needles and stronger thread; and do not push the needles too far into the flesh or skin, lest they tear the wound before it is fully healed; and if you are sewing up a large wound, leave the needle in place while you dress the patient; then take two needles and insert them from one side of the wound to the other as if you were sewing a shirt; then tie these two needles together at their points, and pass them under the first stitch, so that they are well hidden; then sew up the wound with these needles, leaving about half an inch between each stitch; this method is good for large wounds, but for smaller ones you should use thinner needles and stronger thread.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine when it had been outside for 22 hours, and the wound was sealed after 15 days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miracle was that he did not die, and I did not treat it with any medicine, for I was in a place where there was no such thing, and I put on cotton wool twice a day over the wound, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two methods of sewing: take the needle and thread from the outside end all the way to the inside; when it has gone through the flesh, turn the thread around so that it comes out on the other side, and tie it in such a way that you are unable to see where the stitch begins and ends, just as the skin-dresser does when he sews fur, and leave the thread hanging on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the sewing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, as Galiens properly describes it, is when there is no wound and the two parts are naturally joined together, and one of the heads is applied to the other head in such a way: pierce an awl or needle through one of the chief hairs near the mirach, and let the two heads remain; then turn the awl and pierce it from the outside part until it reaches the inside at the two heads; then pierce each of them from the outside part until it reaches the inside, in the two other heads that are on the other side; and this is the mudred method of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says this, and no one testifies against it, that you must sew the belly to two needles, or thread in each; and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the way of those who sew with corroding needles; and know that when the rupture is deep in the belly, this sewing is more painful than that of the other belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	As for the judgment of the wound, it is the same as for other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, as well as the flesh has been moved, if you remove the intestine, and wipe off the blood; then put on the powder while wet, and if the flesh has been moved, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; and pluck out the hair, and let the sinews be tied, and the mirror; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it starts to heal, cotton wool, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called "jeun", cannot heal when they are torn, and this is because of the location of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and because their nature is close to that of infants.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the arrow jumps out of the wound, put it back behind as well as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turning towards yellow or black, you must find the place that is black, from which no blood comes, because there are veins and arteries; then cut between the ties, and hang the two heads down from the side of the wound all the way to the back in order to ease the extraction when the arrow jumps out, and let the wound bleed.
de la routure dou boueil	from the laceration of the bowie
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, you can restore it in some places, because I have seen that a certain man was navered or stabbed with a sword; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became swollen and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and wind; I put on cure according to what I could find, and did not cease to be subtle until it was healed, and I sewed up the leaks.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sewn up, I doubted that the patient had done him harm to his belly; and there was no harm, but he remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and none of the experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, that he must be tied up in some way: take twine from big testicles, then gather the lips of the wound together, and when the twine has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that he can draw his mouth away; and then he covers the head, and this remains so that he cannot untie it, and then he puts another twine after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed up; and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief wound is in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie up the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in some way: take the end of this thread of intestine that has been carefully stripped off, and then tie it to the end of another fine twine made from linen thread, then wrap the thread around the needle, and sew up the intestine, and cut it back at the tear; and this method of sewing with twine is only good in accordance with the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, there is no question but that subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That said, all wounds and abscesses, once they have healed, are called "fistula" in general, and even more so when they have dried up and cracked open.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green medical book, hard and white, where there is no pain, and it also dries up like a bird's feather; and it never breaks all at once, but sometimes thick and sometimes thin; nor does it break easily, and I have already spoken about the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no wound, except by one of the VIII causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or corruption; or because of its malice; or because there is something hard inside, and on the lips, which does not allow it to break; or because there is too much wax; or because the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or because the medicine is not good in the cure; or because what corrupts is a pestilence in nature; or because digestion is late in that region, and health is late, and disappears by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to make known to you the cure of fistula, which is done by work with hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas may occur in all limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sinus, or intestine, or bladder, or some of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes that it touches the principle limb, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of great difficult treatment, and there is no labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the principle limb, and you have engaged to cure it, and you have recognized it, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, reach for it; and if the fistula is bent, reach for it with a slender tent of pliable metal, for the plies bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has broken hands, and you cannot recognize it well with tents, then make it leak with one of the breaks, because it moistens so much from one break to another, and cleans itself; then recognize it carefully with your power, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and it is completely healed, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand upon it, and the place where he feels it; and when you have truly recognized the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then recognize it according to what I have said, and open up the corruption and rotten things that are within; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right side, it is necessary for you to recognize it completely, as much as you can, then put wet tents in medicine water, and bottle them up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrode the excess that is reserved at the bottom; and then put oilmens in janrapping medicine, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted because of the fistula, then recognize it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If in the middle of the night you feel a sharp pain in your main members, as we have said before; and if your nose is covered, and there is decay and darkness, then keep the king until all the decay is gone, then heal with medicines that hinder harm as long as he is healthy; and if he is not healthy, let him lie down as before, knowing that you have not yet arrived: if you discover it and want to get up, wait until you are at the bottom of it, and take out all the decay, then restore the joint; and if it is sound there, then it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too complete that you cannot come there; if there is no other problem except to ease nature; and if there is one small rotten bone, and you can pull it out with pliers, if you extract it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, and if the moisture makes you opposite, and there is no error or fear, then cut and moisten and heal; and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put something on the wound that will cause pus, and let it remain as long as the pores are filled with pus between the bones, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, then keep the corruption for so long that all the bone turns black, then treat the wound; and if there is a lot of decay and it comes down to the root of the bone; then bind it up completely until the decay has been stopped, and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from an inner cause that brought the matter to his leg, and he developed a large abscess, and there was no obvious reason for it to open; but because of their foolishness they caused the abscess to open so much that it corroded much material, and became a fistula, and it came to the point that everyone had an attack of fever and moistening of the body; and many times I saw him being cured after two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being cured, and what was corroding through the fistula to a great extent; and the color of his leg became red, and had a yellow-orange color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of those openings and then searched all the openings and found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and filled one of the openings with as much as I could discover of the bone, and found it corroded and pierced, and the corruption extended inward from the bone; I realized what the bone looked like from the outside, and made sure there was no further corruption, except for that which I had seen; and then I began to treat the wound with medicines over a long period of time, and it would not bind; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuing corruption in the bone, and realized it, and then broke it, and leaned forward to bind the opening; but I only managed to fill about a palm's width of the bone with my hand, and then I stopped; afterwards I bound it with medicines; and it healed and bound firmly, and did not require to be renewed except out of fear for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and out of fear of death which I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car por l'evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l'os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n'ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l'aleir ne a venir.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the trunk, then it shall be handled in such a way: take the thread, and draw it at the head of the bone which is open, and command that he stretch it upwards; and put another thread, thicker than the first, on top of the thread which is stretching upward, and secure them both together, so that you can pull out the broken part, and uncover the bone below where it needs to be pulled, so that the thread does not tear the bone; and put a fire or a hot rock on top of the bone to heat it up; and as long as one can see and feel the corruption, stretch it again. And stretch it another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open anymore, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole arm; then put a hot brand on it, and then silk from one part to the other of the corruption, and let the silk come out of the long side of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then break the joint corrupted, and let the silk go into the bone or into which it belongs from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other injury except at the end; and if the corruption is at the hand's grip, or at the grip of the foot, then it is very bad, but nevertheless you should ask about that corrosion how it opens; and purify it with all means that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not oppose it to you; and know that the chisel and the silks to cover these bones are many, according to the bone's sitting and appearance of the bones, and their size and subtility, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this it is necessary to prepare the instrument for each appearance of work, and know that the work will show you the instrument with which you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument in which you are needed according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if it is due to moisture or due to a fall; and when you have applied the medicine of that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit, then cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from this by fire, or by evil, which is greater, of the failure of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, as if they were burned by fire, and then that corrosion moves from one member to another, taking hold throughout the body; if you hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the percussion of some poisonous beasts, such as sea scorpions and snakes and similar things, if the corrosion is at the top of the two, then cover it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.

And if the pain comes when you work, then cauterize the place thoroughly, or put on some binding powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then tie the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healthy; and I will tell you what happened to the man at home in some detail: he got a blackening that looked like burning from fire, and this corrosion came first on its due course of the foot, so that it discolored all the foot; and when the honorable man saw the corrosion, then he covered his foot with copper, and was cured; and after a long time the corrosion returned to the second joint of the hand, and came to me, and I put things that rub after cleansing the cors, and could not stop the corrosions; and he thought that I should cut off his hand, and I did not want that, that I had hope to reflect the matter; and also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he was desperate completely, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with copper, and was cured; and I have heard only that one should do the other if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption. Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are certain that the skin will toughen, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is like a carriage cover, then you use Egyptian medicine made in this way: take olive oil, and alum, and equal parts, and put the skin in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red, and thickens as well; and then you take it out of the water, and squeeze it; do this seven times, until the skin is very hard, and the wound has healed; and never use water from ashes when this medicine is not present, but you squeeze ashes from a vine branch, and pour water on them, and let it run off, and clisterize it, as long as you know that the skin is well healed; and if the patient cannot endure the pain, or Egyptian medicine or water from ashes does not suit him, then clistere made of honey and wine, where honey has the property to heal and wash, and wine makes one healthy; and when you have done this, and are certain that the skin is well healed, if you clisterize it with this medicine, and it toughens the skin, and you squeeze it into plaster, and make it with olive oil and wine; or you clisterize it with various medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the section on the treatment of ointments; and if the wound is small, and the clistere cannot enter, then you widen it a little with iron, and put a tent of the Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it has widened; and if the wound is too wide, then you leave it open where the clistere can enter, and if the opening where the bowels come out is above, then you make it lower, and if it is below, then you raise it higher.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is in perfect shape, do not leave it hanging; and if you cannot cover the breast with it as you see, arrange it in such a way that the bow runs down to the lowest point it can reach, for when the bow is in perfect shape, do not leave it hanging; and if you cannot cover the breast with it as you see, arrange it in such a way: that the bow runs lightly downward, leaving nothing of the bow; and take medicines that strengthen it to be placed over the chest, and wrap them in linen cloths that cover all the chest; then cover them tightly at the top where the opening is slightly larger than the first, since ointments are applied on another cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and put it on the chest opening to tighten the bow, and do not take off the large cloth except after many days once; and he who is on the chest opening, often takes it off to take off the bow, and knows what runs from the bow, if it is poison or blood or enough or digested or undigested; and take care that the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and how your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that flows on the chest opening, know that the breasts are beginning to feel warm, and approach them; and then unbind them in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, if you change another cloth, renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become swollen and uncomfortable after many days, know that the breasts do not ache.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison enters slowly over a long time, then do not despair of health, for the health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toe of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A bunion is an aposteme that grows out of the joint of the thumb from the base of the hand, or from the foot, or perhaps in another two; and when it has grown out, and no care is taken, then it comes to form a bunion, and it becomes hard and hot so much that there is pain in it, and the joint becomes large, and its color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it then as we said in the section on treatment, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the surplus that has been left of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; but if the nail presses into the flesh, and irritates it, then you must take off the nail that presses, and cut it short, and lightly burn the edge with fire, and put on medicines that are hot and corrosive to remove it all; and then treat it with oil until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et si la corruption est dans l'os, alors le coupe, et traitant-le fermement, car tant que l'os est corrompu, il ne peut guérir ; et si tu vois la corruption doubler, alors le coupe selon ce qui a été dit ci-dessus, puis guéris-le tant qu'il soit guéri ; et s'il est brulé et enflé et sent une grande douleur, alors il convient que tu le guérisses en premier ; puis coupe l'ongle avec le couteau de façon transversale au-dessus, et veille à ce que la lame ne coupe pas au-delà du lit de l'ongle, car le patient ressentrait trop de douleur ; et s'il arrive, alors place quelque chose qui apaise.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	La douleur des doigts de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Les deux doigts qui naissent dans les mains de certains hommes sont parfois charnus, parfois osseux, et n'ont jamais d'ongles, et aucune racine de doigt ne naît dans certains de ces cas.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cil who is born of two roots shall not move, and cil who is born of a joint of two roots, by chance shall move; the size of that which is charnus is so light, in some way: measure it at its root with a broad spatulate.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Cil who is born at the root of the joint must be carefully treated: if you hold him by the cup.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or should be at the root of the derrièment, it is fitting that you first cap the heart completely up to the bone, then cap the bone with a suitable thread, and then treat it until it is well.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints which come together by nature, by the joining of a wound, or by the burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you cap that which is joined by nature, according to its natural forms; then place between two pieces of thin cloth soaked in oil rosin, so that it does not join; or place between two pieces of fine linen, until the joints are joined, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Se soudemens comes to neither of its two with the palm, if grip it firmly as it should.
des vils	of ill-reputed
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The vis are large and wrapped in a thick, melanolic skin, which causes numerous members of the body to suffer; and as for those who walk on their feet and work and carry loads, they suffer more than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not administer any poultices, and then cure it from the base.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure with iron should be done according to two methods: one is that of applying poultices, and then drawing out the black blood; and another method is that of lifting the vein up, and drawing it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting should be done according to this method: first, raise the leg of the healthy person with very hot water, until the large veins are slightly visible, then extract the leg of the sick person from above the knee down to the ankle; then cut the vein open in one place, or two, or three, wide enough, and draw out the blood little by little at your hand, as much as the sick person can bear it; and then bandage him, and order him that he color his meat with black dye; and then start again with the evacuation and cure when the veins are clear, and bandage the person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation of the text: 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if it is twisted and bent and wrapped up together, and it is not straightened, as we have said, then you should break it cruelly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And the shape of iron that one covers over the vis if it is curved, and does not cut it, so that it covers the vein; and it is a thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but being thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where no herbs or trees grow, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this leads to skin rot that comes from within the body, spiraling between the skin and the bone.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of this injury are that an extremely large inflammation has come to the leg, then the joints change, and the injury begins to grow out, just as a root does from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And if the joints open up, then you wrap a piece of cloth from one-and-a-half to two inches long around each, and tie it, and leave the cloth hanging down the leg, and every time it comes loose, if the cloth is too long, cut off a part and wrap the rest, but do not cover it over its root, until it is all gone; for if you cover it, it will enter into the shell and bring about abscesses and rottenness where it is; so that this injury should be dealt with little by little until it is done, and leave nothing behind except a scar; and this chapter has been treated from five to ten handspan, and when you cut it, if it comes off easily or is bent, and pierces all the way down, so that everything inside is gone; and have medicines applied to it daily that cause rottenness, then heal it just as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at no time to this vein with hands, and least when it opens in the joint of the foot, or where the foot is, and there comes a great loss, and from which rain falls; so then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the worms that are born between the hide and the cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buff disease," because it often affects buffaloes, and it is a small worm that born between the hide and the cart, and goes everywhere ascending and descending, and feels well at the touch of one member to another, until it comes off the skin where it has gone, and disappears; and it is infected with some kind of pus, as if it came from worms and snakes and beetles and parasites, and doubts about its malice, because when it goes through the body, and reaches the head, and comes to the eye, sometimes enters, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him recover and be drawn out, only then can we go: so it is necessary that you place the joint in its proper position and fix it with a strong and tight ligature; then lift up and draw out forcefully, and let his head fall perfectly into the bed, and if you do not see it, fire cauterize him from above until he dies; and the greatest damage he does is that he corronts the oil, as we have said; and if you see him coming with his head near the oil, then you should strain out his hair completely, then lift up, and draw out forcefully. And it is necessary to use the patient for the cleaning of the skin of medicines that dissolve bad humors, and sear himself with meat that is rotting.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members, and moves from member to member; and I have seen this one that I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to see a sick woman, and I uncovered her arms, and saw a small swelling in the vein of her arms; and immediately it felt like a worm going into her shoulder, sooner than anything else, as if it were quicksilver when it passed from one place to another; the pain left that place, and went into her shoulder, and then after a little while corrupted throughout her whole body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she was turning in bed again, as I had seen her do.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how much this woman moved her limbs from one member to another, for I have never seen such a thing with this disease.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Anyway, I have seen many people whose bodies move from one place to another with pain, but I have never seen such a thing as with this woman; and I thought that perhaps she had a tight body and her veins uncovered, and because of the constriction of wind that appeared; and I did not see it for this reason in those who are thin, and whose bodies and veins are relaxed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to heal this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens like we have said, tie above and below, and then cover as much as the constriction allows; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see blood in your eyes, if you treat with pills of putrid garlic, and pills of serapin, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	are various, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body where they come from.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	have various shapes, as there are some with large points, small ones, curly ones, and those that are souded; and some have II angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and one that does not come from any member at all sometimes comes out according to II ways: or in a principal member it comes out like a brain, an ear, a liver, a pancreas, a rein, an intestine, a bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she dies and does not feel any of the members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you after, then you know: if it is necessary for you to remove this arrow, because death comes after many dispositions; and when that bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not perfectly taken out, then you draw it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the arrow pierces and makes the bone ache, and the medicine that is on top of the skull, and when there is paralysis and weakness and turning and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness in the tongue, and spasms and confusion of thought, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps it does not come out through the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses its speech and voice; and when that wound becomes wet and white like pus, and looks like fire; and if you notice this sign, then take care of it, and extract the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the sneeze when it comes is that it is near the left breast, and also feels as if it were wedged against something hard, not empty; and perhaps the sneeze also moves like the hairs, with a short pause in the middle, and then coldness and perspiration come, and fainting: so one knows that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the sneeze that does not bode well is that there is a sudden loss of consciousness and foam jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he gasps for air and feels cold all over.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the sneeze comes in the cover of the back, it is a sign of delirience and great pain and sighing and movement of all the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the sneeze comes from the belly, perhaps it is a sign that something indigestible has come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters through the belly, and does not go out through the intestines, there is no hope for the patient's recovery or for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters into the bladder, and the urine flows out in spurts and goes away, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if as it happens and the neck and throat and shoulder and aid and spine and chest and legs, and the limb in question, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the neck or the artery, and it does not come out, then as I will tell you what happened to me, do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me that an arrow entered into the throat at the root of the neck: I tried to take it out, and pulled it from the other side of the fat of the ear, and was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And throw an arrow that it enters the fat of the oil desoz the papeir desoz, and the arrow was re-set, and I could not get anything but the tip towards the furst, and the arrow was big of a turquiose arc, all I fer legier without ears; the game was sanez, and no came any bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I threw an arrow into the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic to ears: I knew the beards, and I delayed as much as I threw it, and the Christians were sane.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I threw an arrow at a man that it entered his cheek or belly, and I thought he died; and then, after XXX days, if he did not return to his condition; I cut on the arrow, and I engaged it, and I threw it again, and did not have any bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you want to go to a man who has an arrow in his chest or back, and the wound is closed with a patch; delay the arrow inside it, and do not change its natural course, nor find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I know another man to whom an arrow has entered his face, and the wound was closed with a patch; and he delayed it in this way so as not to suffer great pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I know a king's man who had an arrow in his neck, and the wound was closed with a patch; it was slightly tilted to the right side; and the patch was all torn up. I was called to heal him after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	There was a very tight wound.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I wanted to give it a long and subtle treatment, and I did not feel it; but he felt pain and prickling in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of an arrow; I put plaster on the wound to stop it from bleeding, so that the blood would not flow; and I saw the wound of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put plaster on it every day, and quickly resolved the wound, and delayed it for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound a corrosive medicine every day until it was open, and tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which was getting stuck at the place; then I removed it from the opening of the wound with a small tool, so that the wound opened; I waited for three months, and then I healed the wound so well that I pulled out the nails on both sides, and they couldn't come out; so I stopped using tools to make things subtle and invent ways to use them, until one day I got it right, so I put it on, and I closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And I saw that the cartilage of his nose could not be restored; but I restored it, and the wound was souded, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	And have you not heard about the quality of extraction of certain arrows, so that you put your cure on what I do not say, for the book cannot take away everything; but the master surgeons deal well with a small amount and with what is present and failing, they bring about nine operations and nine instruments to the dismemberment of strange things that come in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows are in the members or they are stuck except according to two ways: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which is stuck by the side where it enters, is an arrow entering into its flesh, and is never stuck at any other time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her leave the hair so long that it is not cut in the middle, and let it grow; and if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let her stay like this for some days, and every day let her move a little; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, pierce it with a fine blade all around, so that the hair inside is stretched, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and comes out at one of the temples, and some of the accidents that I have said can happen to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days, because if the arrow comes out only halfway, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and not out, and does not come out until it reaches the temple, and the patient remains for some days without any bad accident, then the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is so stuck in here that it cannot be removed, then you should administer tar like I told you; and then treat the joint as long as it is healthy.

The patient who is free of disease has no definite limit, but when fasting or eating, at all hours and in all seasons; nor should physicians treat children under the age of XIIII years, nor women after giving birth for only four months up to seven months. Nor should old people over the age of LX years be treated.
