Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When treating a patient, in any way, it is necessary to determine that there is no obstruction in the intestines of a light enema, if there has been a retention of stool, so that the veins do not attract the excess waste that is harmful to the main organs; nor should one treat someone who is too ill from meat, or alcohol, as long as it lasts, nor those who are dry due to sickness; and if one wants to treat after a colic passion, vomiting, stomach cramping, excessive sexual activity, heavy labor, staying up late, fasting, or drinking, or taking medicines, then do so with caution; then bath or swimming, if it does not harm them, for the subtle humors of the body, and let him gain weight, through food, drinks, and medicines, if necessary; then between bath or swim, because the heat subtilely affects the blood, and treat from the third day, as we have said; and avoid work, drinking, luxury, and similar things; be quiet and calm, and let the healer be higher than the one who treats, and rub his arms twice or three times, then stretch the vein gently, because if it is too constricted or tight, it cannot move; and then rub the patient's skin with his left hand in the area of the vein that needs to be stretched, a little at a time, so that the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the healer's hand with the flame of a small bowl of old oil, and place his right hand on the patient's skin where the vein needs to be stretched, so that the vein does not hurt or cause pain.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run as cords along the body, and some of these are prone to windiness; so when placed on fire, if removed from fire, they cannot be opened, and so are those; and if the vein is opened, too much pressure must be applied, for the surgeon must be cautious about such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, that is good; but if not, let it be done again a little later in a place of healing or in bed, if the veins are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are swollen, and the patient hopes for it, let him rest a day or two, and do not tie the arm: perhaps it will come to naught; but if you doubt that it may not hurt as much as you see, then set fire to the whole limb properly; and work at the wound with care, so that the veins are not injured, for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the wound bleeding, do not recommend any medicine, and put a little oil on it, because it heals the wound quickly, and is soft in this place where the oil is; and thus administer the oil to each wound that you heal the veins for stopping the flow of blood; and that one does also make three times as hard and bent when put on the wound; but too much subdue it, if it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there is a large abscess that often occurs, most especially when the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry and put a wet sponge on the wound and bind it tight for an hour; and it is good that after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains at the place for several days without turning black or green, then do not worry about it; and if you see it, put some aloe or mirrremade with calament juice, monstere, or similar on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance happen in the hand of the patient under pressure from his hand; therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the soft place under pressure from your hand, then that is the appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then know that you do not put anything on what we have said, for perhaps in the cort there is no artery; but he makes it dry to harden the place, then he cures it with other remedies, until he is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And each person takes the blood according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if his blood is black, so let it out until it is red; and if you see him fat, so let it out until it is thin; and if he is too hot, so let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is suitable for him who is thin and out of shape, and has the need to extract blood, that he make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits him to heal little by little, and let him heal by cutting across, not by piercing; and this method of healing is saved from the corruption of blood and the tangling of nerves, and is better than the healing of the long, large wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose hearts are in need of healing, it is appropriate to give moist bread made with grape juice; if it is heated, it should be eaten three or four times a day. And if the person's complexion is cold, then before eating the moist bread, it should be dipped in muscatel syrup or in honey syrup with aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and caraway, and in sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if they have a fever at the beginning of their sickness, after drinking three or four glasses of water, it is appropriate that they drink a broth and muscatel syrup, and aromatic syrup made with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and caraway, and sweet-smelling syrups, and use other things that we have mentioned in the chapter on the treatment of syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if they vomit up food and then eat again later on, but are weakened by great sickness, that they be healed little by little according to the quantity of its continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to vomit his arms after the first saigne, and he has a strong heart, so he saignes seven hours after the first saigne, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another place, should bleed the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has blood within the body that is already warmed up, and causes fever; so, when a large quantity comes out, and widens the opening so much that it sounds like a bell; then you should adjust all conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse when he bleeds, so that death does not come from the opening, and this happens many times, when the bleeding is neglected; and you must not untie the arm, and make the blood come out again, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly on it; nor if it is bent, let it extend the arm generously, for that would be bad; but leave it until it bleeds the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, as much as the blood that is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out, and put a little rope soaked in water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is still bleeding, let it be and do not constrict it, as long as the abscess is subsiding.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires that the blood be drained a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is cut from the arm at the base of the wrist; for this is a composed vein.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of the cut is such that the patient holds his hand in hot water until it becomes red; then let it be moved gently, so that the vein appears clearly, then cut it across, not wide nor long; and if it should be torn, and the cut be near the joint of the hand, do not put it back into the hot water again, for we put it back more in haste than in rest; and this cut from this vein is more secure than all other veins, for it neither hurts the artery nor the nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment for the right hand's salve is to all liver diseases, and this is how: draw out the hand, and dip it in hot water until the vein is gone, if you can see it; and then, if you cut across it, do not harm anything completely; and do not cut too much completely, because the nerves are all exposed; then put back the hand in hot water; if it has frozen into the wound, it cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if it is necessary to put oil and thread on it to join it firmly together, do so with each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment for the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do all the same as I have told you above for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The doctor treats the disease of the spine by applying fire to it; as for the disease of the leg, he applies fire to it and burns it, and does not leave a scar. The disease of the leg may be treated by a hot iron if there is no pain or swelling. Fire is used to treat a broken bone that is out of place and causing pain.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	The quality of the doctor's treatment is that the patient should dip his foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it stops hurting, and put it on the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go more rains; heal wherever there is a larger rain, or at the ankle, that must be used.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are out of place, and treat it across as well as down; and let the flames not go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get out of it, put the foot into water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if he is injured for the first time, then start the second time above a little, because the leg is salty; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and in this way make the sound of the other leg even.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic vein is at the ankle and its injury deserves the pain of the thigh when it is for a wound.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this injury is that the patient goes into or out of the bath, and draws it up from the ankle with four twists, because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then heal it in all ways that you can, and go through it; and cut it more than you do, for the leg is swollen, and it is very relented.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't let him go out in the rain or in the sun, and towards the small two, and protect yourself from the wind; and make the blood run until you see it, and then remove the bandage, and put cotton on it and tie it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Healing with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Are made of horns, or of air, or of glass; and ventilation is done according to two ways: by injuring and drawing blood, or without injuring.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventilation that does not hurt is done in 12 ways of the body: one at the top of the head; and another at the back; and another along both sides of the neck; and another at the mouth; and another at the two arms; and another at the two legs; and another at the two feet; and ventilation does not treat blood except for small veins that are scattered in the chest, and therefore it does not hurt anyone, neither by hot nor cold, in any illness that comes from excess unless all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if because of the necessity of sickness one must ventose, or by habit, if we administer it every hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each ten; for there are such who, when they have to ventose, become very heavy; and those who come out with a swollen face, and with a swollen head, and with a swollen neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who come out with a drop of blood in their mouth, and have slipped the tongue, and thirst for blood; and if there are those who dream, and see by lack of blood and navel and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and in particular when it is mid-month, we order them to ventose after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The surgeon of the museum helped in the headache of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and should not come until the whole body has been evacuated; and this ventosis is in the place of the headache of the cephalic, and should not come except for those of a cold complexion who are using or have had a fever, because it does them great harm; and for this one should not come at night when using, nor those who have a cold head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover often from it, if they become dizzy, and because of this, the suction cup should be placed a little further down due to the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And the suction should be placed in the neck area where the pain is located and where the windpipe and larynx are, and because of this, it can help with strangle throat, a cut in the trachea, and nausea and stomach upset; but it should be pressed lightly, for if it is pressed too hard, it may cause dizziness or upset the stomach.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And the suction should be placed in the neck area where the pain is located and where the windpipe and larynx are, and because of this, it can help with strangle throat, a cut in the trachea, and nausea and stomach upset; but it should be pressed lightly, for if it is pressed too hard, it may cause dizziness or upset the stomach. Tell the patient to express their hand so that they don't crush the artery and prevent the flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings of the mouth cause disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; it is at the level of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders cause a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the arms cause as much pain as three veins in the arms, because they hurt a lot; and instruct the patient that he not make too much noise, because the bones are naked and there are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The windings that are on the back cause hemorrhoids at the fundament, and similar diseases, and it is necessary that the winding be big and of iron, so that it can well milk; and by chance, if it were too subtle, it would break, and would make big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Legs' suction cups if they open up wide, for they draw blood from all the body, and are like the old pains of the rain, and of the mare, and of the bladder, and make flowers come back; and they are in the place of the two sophenes, and of the two feet, but nevertheless they weaken the body after a long time, and cause death in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method for applying the suction cups to the legs is that you put them first where they are open, and suck them quickly, and place them firmly, and move them evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then go on, and remove the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some who have very tender skin, and clear pores: so it is necessary to wound them once only, and to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the man is fat outside, he should be struck twice: once to soften the path of the blood that is thick.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the man is very fat, he should be struck three times; and when we want to squeeze out blood little by little, we should press only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw blood, we should do so frequently; and if the man is fat, he should be struck thoroughly, and the ends should be such that the wound be suddenly seen, and cover with oil of mint, or of sweet almonds, or of pumpkin seed, and if it is in summer, with oil of watercress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the man's surplus is thick and cold, take oil of bitter almonds, or of balsamite, or oil of fennel, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if to someone who has a sore that is tender and full of pus, there is no need to put oil on it, but it needs to be washed after the rise of the rose water, or cold water, or morel water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if one has moisture, if it rises so, or with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And if one has large superfluity, they rise with old wine, or with water of oak, or with a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar; and it is not necessary to clean with the vacuum before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and they should not fall asleep after the vacuum, but when they need to vacuum, as soon as they are vacuumed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are healing are coleric, and the sun is too sharp and inflamed; so it is necessary that he take cold things, as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with the ashes, and similar things; and little fish, and cart of char, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should drink syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and little fish, and cart of char, and moist meats. And the day that he is windblown, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give certain men three times or musk before or after ventosation, to strengthen the main members; and make the sun subtile, but it is not necessary to drink it if he is hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The ventilations that do not hurt are those placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and podagre, and on the belly and the boughs and the rains and the hunchback, because this member does not suffer to be hurt on the outsides, and it is only done to attract blood from one member to another, as when we put ventilations on the breasts when the sick person is not well; to remove the viscous substance that is in the member, as when we put ventilations on the belly and the boughs to weaken the member; and to remove the pain, when there is an operation or a stone, so it removes the operation, or deserts the stone from its place; and thus it is done when one puts them on the liver and on the mouse when there is retained ventosity, and these ventilations are empty, minished only for sucking so much; and they are never combined together again, nor plainness of fresh water, as in the disease of pleurisy, and in such a way that the ventilation is filled with hot water or water in which he has cooked herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup, administered to fire thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It should be two inches wide and half a palm in circumference, and have a small hole in the center about the size of a needle, so that it does not hurt the patient when applied to the limb; and in the middle a rod of wood or iron, for a grip, and there are large and small ones depending on the disease and age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of thin people are different from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And it should be placed on the limb like this: take the grip of wax or thread, and put it in the middle of the suction cup over the rod that is in the middle of the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and the two are on the hole that we have said, so that when you remove it, the vapor comes out, and then take off the suction cup; and take the grip again as before, and renew it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is used to treat pleurisy, there is no water, no fork or piercing, and it is only useful when it is dry, and is placed on the limb with a slight force; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	The suction cups that are used to treat pleurisy have no water, no fork or piercing, and they are only useful when they are dry, and are placed on the limb with a slight force; and this is the form: Suction cups should be used only for small limbs, like lips and gums, and similar things; and in the case of a horse's jaw, if it is necessary to use them, then they should be placed in sweet water, until they are free of wind and clear; and then, if it is possible to put suction cups on the jaw, they should be put there, because this is better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the joint, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the joint is very sore after the heart of the veins, so wet a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the vein is blocked; and if the veins are many, put on vitriolic powder, or gall, and similar things, until they are blocked; or you put half a handful of peeled peas on the joint, and let them sit until they burn into the joint, so they will now block; and if you need to do more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the veins do not want to come together, then rub the joint with fresh blood, or you put an needle in it as long as a vein comes out of it, and then put them on, and sometimes when they feel the blood, they burn; and when you see that they are peeing, then sprinkle on a little powder of aloes and sepalum, or of ash, so they will now pee.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The art of chemistry is often necessary in the practice of medicine, and is useful for the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know then, dear son, that the wise men have poured this chemistry over, which has never been found in any of the old books or letters; and for this reason the science is strange to our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing except what I learned from the study of the old books, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have condensed it into a summary form at the end, and have clearly set forth the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters where wisdom is placed, and pause on truthfulness so that those who test it know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a fracture or dislocation or twist or break in anyone, it is fitting that you hurry to save the sick person on both sides, if no harm has befallen him, i.e. if he is not weak of heart, or old; or if his bones are not too thin, or too often broken; and do not drink too much cold juice, nor eat any fat foods, and do not fill yourself with too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the temperature of the appendix, nor the expansion of matter in the limb; then bring back the disease to its first government which it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed with meat which is fat, or with viscosity, like cooked flour in water, and rice, and testicles, and pies, and eggs of fish, and fresh fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a slow nutrition will delay the healing of the fracture and hasten it more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people can not well heal or knit together according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, like the bones of small children; but rather cure them with great fat meat which hardens and joins the limb together, as much as it will, and then stop eating it all, and for this purpose it is necessary to feed on large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the shoulder, and another by cutting, so as to form the shape of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that makes a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each kind is its tool for restoration, according to what the memory comes in place; and it is known the break of the bone by what the turn is crooked, and open well by the side, and a bit on the presser of the hand; and when there is no twisting or breaking, and the patient does not feel much pain, it is not because there is no break, but it may have twisting, or a slit, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it by hand, but put medicine on it that comes here later, and then now hold it gently in place.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that comes in the arm, and there are two parts separated, now put them to be even, so that an abscess is born and a scar comes out, if you leave it for a day, as long as the abscess is calmed down; then he puts it evenly on the muscle that you can move easily and carefully, and know that the restoration of him is easier than the restoration of the one who has pieces; then hold it in place, just as it is written later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces of bone in the hand or foot, or in a small member, or in two cords, or in one cord and in your hand; put the member back in its natural position, so that when the parts of the broken member are healed, you remove all additions to their places at the muscle that you can move it, and keep from your work so that no damage or pain comes to the patient; and fit the two bones well according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel the pulse well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if the dressing is done well, and do not squeeze it too much, do not press it as those who make it come by their work heat and contraction of the member do, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, teach the patient that he not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, turning or in any other way; and guard well that the member be so secure that he feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and the position in which you put it should not cause him any pain; and be careful that it is put correctly, so that there is no twistedness when he is restored; and the quality of the member is according to what I told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken member are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arm and leg and other parts: it is convenient to wrap linens of linen and fine fabric; and those that are large, such as thigh and calf: it is convenient to wrap with a broad and sturdy linen, for the broad linings embrace all the large member and hold it tight on all sides so that there is no gap; then remove light stitches, three or four times according to the member, and hold a hand on all the lining, then go up over the break and hold it less, so that the break moves a little; and soften the lining a little and a little, until you press most of the blood from the place of injury, then take another lining, and turn it again over the injured part; then return to the other side of the break, and hold it gently, not too hard or too gently, as we have said in the first line of thread above; then put the linings between the linen or cloth stitches, so that they are all equal, then tie them all together on top of the bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or abscess, place over it a warm compress, and let it rest in this way for some days; then draw up onto your fingers, and be of half a length of a wide cane treated with salt, or of a twig from which one makes cleats, or of palms, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And the stake that one puts over the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and be also as far away from the member as it is necessary in size or length; then draw up onto the stakes as you did at first, then tie it together, like you did with the first stake; the smaller it is, the better; and the thread should be fine, not too thick or too thin, and made of linen; for if the thread is thick, like those foolish people who make their ligatures out of linement rope, it is a great mistake, because the ligature will not be equal if it is too thin, and it only deserves to be less than two inches between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pregnant by the legs of the stars after extraction in her healthy days, then let them be covered with linen, or another rag, so that they do not scar.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breach, and the cure is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not suit to extract stars from all the members the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are large, it does not suit to put stars before five or seven days, or more according to the urgency of the abscess; and here is the way of the ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour which sticks to the walls of the mill, and confound it with much egg, and put this confection, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and that is the common way of the plasterer restoring fracture in many conditions, and most of all in women and small children, for it is not suitable to be too soft or too hard.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other ways to make plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take aloes and myrrh and nettle and asafetida and arabic gum and mugwort, 10; mirth andaloes, 5; alchemi, 8; and make a powder of them, and mix it with sheep's dung; the mixture should be warm, for it is good composition, and will quickly restore broken bones, and is useful to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make plaster for healing twists: take mugwort and castor oil, 10; myrrh and aloes, 7; acacia, 6; and bolete armenia, 10; grind them well, and mix with sharp or sheep's dung, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to make plaster for joints and bones that have come out of place, to soothe the pain immediately, and to treat fractures: take fresh lamb's skin, and soak it in warm water and cooked oil, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	It is good for soothing an abscess, and properly taking away the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making an ointment to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth hazel leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of making an ointment for healing broken bones and reducing the inflammation of an abscess: take dried leaves of the fig tree and earth hazel leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallow, chamomile flowers, violets, flour of vetches, a part of each; grind them and confer with wine, and heat the members, and confer with water or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making an ointment that is more powerful than the first method, to be used when a persistent abscess develops before healing the broken bone.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mullein, and seed of flax, thistle, meadwort, and fennel, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part or the other; and grind, and confect with vinegar of salt, or with sweet vinegar, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book he says that one should not put anything on a broken limb for healing except wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to me that one should put on a broken limb things dry and slightly warm, such as mirr and allspice and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plasters for lesions and pain: take sheep's wool, or goose feathers, and mullein, and yarn of even length, and grind them, and make a plaster with it, and apply it to the member.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor does his bone move from its place; but if pain comes to its place, or itching, lack of rest, or swelling, you are in a hurry, and loosen it, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge moist with sea water, and dip into the water, and raise the member up, until the itching stops, and the pain is calmed down; then let the member rest for an hour, and then put on another dry one, wet it with water or oil and tie it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm; and ease the inflammation of the member, and calm the pain, and then begin again with the gentle application, and a little bit of plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and swollen and painful and inflamed throughout, and you need to use plaster and binding, if it worsens, as you did at first, with equal care.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb at all as we have said, if it is not bound up after three days or four or five or seven; and never leaves it more than 20 days, according to what can be seen, until the break comes and approaches the joint of the wood; then restrain it more than before, and make its flesh grow thicker, as I have said before; and if you see that it is drying up more than is necessary, then immediately pour hot water on it, every time you release it, and let it be for each third day, and wash a little of the lye; by this work therefore restrain the swelling to the limb, and carefully break down what has been misaligned: this is bad, and if it is painful and fearful ovraiges, and I do not see anything else that can make it stronger and bring it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various methods of breaking.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many different ways to break it, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there is a break that is made from the impact of an axe, and the collar bone is all the way down to the bone, so as to have made one like this; and this way of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	For the spear breaks the bone from above without piercing it, and this way of breaking is called "absolue"; and the wound caused by these two great breaks or a small one.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a break due to an axe head, or a sword cut, or a collar bone from stone, or falling on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating break, which approaches the skin but does not go through it, or which is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that has entered the bone is as fine as a hair, and for this reason is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made by a stone, or by a blow, or by a similar thing, and enters the bone, and the hole is as big as a hair, just as the blacksmith does when he hammers on the bellows; then it goes into the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if there is more moisture under the cheekbone, so that it becomes soft like a child's; and there are all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are made from, just as they are made from stapes; and I will speak about their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the investigation at tents, and by the cart corrupted that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is made by what when one has discovered the bone, and frots it up, if so opens the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for the fracture, take care as to the accidents of the disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, palmations, feverish ague, and the hair coming out and reddening, and other similar things in various dispositions, so cannot he healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeful accident, and expect salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the birth comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourth day at most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue that covers the bone does not rot, and comes the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the skull, so it is necessary that you split the damaged part inwardly; and it is necessary that you press the chief on the patient's head, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if the blood comes out at the uncovering of the bone or abscess, help him with what is appropriate, and it is necessary that you fill the place with wet towels soaked in oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and be sure about the blood coming out; then begin to split the bone, and this is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you split the narrow end first, and that is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I another way more big than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different taillemens, some are narrow and others are wide, and are pointed, and are made of iron; and work lightly, so that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, then it is necessary that you pierce it through, so that taillemens with barres do not completely go through the bone, but leave a margin or circle above the tip that does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes in its place at the end of the bone, so that you have barres for all tests; and this is the form of the three ways of making barres:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce through the bone is that you put the barres on top of the bone, and turn it back with your fingers until you feel that the bone has been pierced; then remove the barres a little further away, and do this everywhere, then cut off the space of the bone that is between the knots, and do this more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you hold the bone in your hand, or at any of the instruments that you have like pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the skull nor the sinews.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have broken the bone and treated it, if you see that you have retained the sharpness of the bone which is distant from all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it should be softer and more delicate than the other incisor; and if it does not retain any small bones or scales, if it has bent slightly on the tools; then cure the wound with the things we mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working which is that of Galen who is more skillful; and work it very hard, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, at which the break is open; so that when you have discovered this part, you shall place the point of this lens-shaped incisor there, from whence it comes:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the part is wet on II sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then pound it lightly with a small mallet all around, and take good care of the piece which is coming off; if it is bent on the bone, then bend the bone lightly, for to break the bone well is not without danger, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce just to the membrane, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, so cover again that sharpness, and remove the scales with a fine razor whose you must have different quantities, to regulate in each place the most appropriate, according to the work and the form of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have a lot of small razors, and then more fine ones, and do not cease to do this as long as it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you regulate according to their alignment; and this is a thing that has not yet been answered to those who have put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the silk is open, you should take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and oil it, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled up in II or III, and oil it with wine and oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not hurt the silk, then cover it up for a day or two, until the abscesses are calmed down, then remove it, and administer medicines as roots, and flour of times, and incense powder, and herbal substances; and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer again medicines that do not sting; and guard so that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave the infection, nor let bowels gather above the membrane, for when the bowels gather over the silk of the skull, if they corrode and perforate, they cause great harm to the patient; because when you put something mordant on the silk, if it seeps through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Guard against, therefore, any bad accident coming to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackening does not come but only because of the medicine that has been put on it, which has its virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glues one cloth, and lay it on the wound; then treat with the methods that seem right to you until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	I tell you that neither of the two bones above it are ever broken if one is separated from the other, for they are two: and that bone is cartilaginous and does not break unless it is forced or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two bones is broken, then you should push your little finger or pin from the nose on that bone, and make it equal to the length of your index finger, and slightly bend it from side to side until the bone regains its natural shape; do this lightly, and guard against the patient feeling pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.
