And if the fracture is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot come to its place, you shall believe that you put it even with the head of a rod not too thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, do so then, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth day, when the abscess is calmed down, then bind at the neck with linen bands, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another on the other side, if it is a fracture; and may the bands be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And do not say that one should moisten the bandages every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that the bandages be wet with oil of olive and powder of molybdenum; then leave the bandage on, until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And there is no need to put goose feathers in the tent, and if it has an inner cover, keep it closed, and let the air out, and let the disease spread among them; or do as I have said.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes out while you are operating, put cotton wet with oil or a string of cotton wool soaked in oil, or a small piece of linen string.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come out, put plaster on it from afar, made of flours of barley and incense powdered with honey, then put light cloths on it, and do not bind the tent; and if the break in the tent is small and it breaks into small pieces, extract them with appropriate tools, then cut off the break, and heal things that have been damaged by water, and always, as for plasters and ointments appropriate to it; and if there is no sore inside the tent, heal the tent, and put sheepskin on it, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very deep, and it is not broken in two, but is bent inward, so that it looks like a hook, then one should carefully adjust it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left side, put your index finger of the right hand inside, gently pushing it back into place, and make it even with the left hand from the outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is in two places, you should carefully adjust it with two extensions, making them even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement is painful, or there is a rupture, then put on the broken jaw a thread of gold, silver, or silk; and put over it two double towels; and put over one a large, well-made plate, or a piece of even leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it tightly with the string, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure is changing, let it rest for three days and then put back what has been changed; and apply plaster, of flour from the mill with a lot of eggs or flour of sesame, after having removed the cerote; and put on another light plaster, and if the plaster starts to dry, and the condition of the patient does not change, let it rest as long as it is healthy; often it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come out, so treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not take a piece of the bone off; if subtle of the osteotomy are the tools suitable for it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have osteotomies all these pieces, and there is no delay at all, if the wound is wide, put on it I with a suitable plaster to prevent infection, until he is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the fire
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	For the fire forceps break many times before, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to III manners: or it is broken and dislocated in II, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the ovraiges is when the break is without wound, that you have II ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the fire break; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make equal the break on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair loss.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	Et s'il a besoin de plus grand soulagement, alors mets une sphère ronde de tissu, ou de laine, sur l'épaule du patient ; ou soit grande selon sa nécessité; et tenez-la fermement, et tirez la sphère à votre main, afin que vous mettiez le désordre égal, comme il convient.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the arm out at the shoulder, so that it comes off perfectly, then it is convenient for the patient to lie down on his side; and put the shoulder out at a slant, and lift up the members with a lever, as much as the bone of the arm will come up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then put the break at your sides, and if you find it too difficult, then split it with a saw; and pull the pieces out lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then take off the tool that you have to one of the incisions, but keep the device on the bone:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and appears like a spoon, and is not a hair, and is also wide as it should be according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and there are two heads, just as you see, one wide and the other small, which corresponds to the rupture of the wound that you made when you fractured the bone; and when you are sure of the warm, if a little wound, and the rupture is small, or if you doubt about it, then cover the wound with cloth and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if warm comes, then wet it with oil and vinegar and wine and put on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if warm comes, then wet it with oil and vinegar and wine and put on it. For the extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and no rupture, do this: Put powder from the mill and ashes of eggshells on the bone, and lightly pack it, and fasten a spittle around the joint, if you need to; then take a very long bandage about a palm wide, and wrap it twice around the packs, and wrap the powder; then take a thin stake three fingers wide and long, and wrap it tightly around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the stake on top of the break, and fasten the stake to the joint; and loosen and tighten it every day, and when you see that the bandage holds well, and you can clearly see that the stake does not move around the bone, then leave it alone for a week or more; and then start wrapping again if you think it is necessary, and fasten it and let it be; and it will be healed in about 28 days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For if the shoulder dislocates and is out of place, and does not move by itself; then adjust it according to its shape and return it to its natural position in all ways that you can; then put on powder from the mill with lots of flour, and light dustings, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and thin board, a little wider than the shoulder, and loosen the board at the edges of the shoulder, so work it with linen thread, so that the board lies evenly; and then tighten it firmly so that the board does not move from its place, and check it every day; and whenever it moves, tighten it again, and make the board even if it has come out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is put back in XX days or xxv, and when this number is complete, then loosen it, and be sure, for it is not bone that comes out easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone projects forward, and does not open the cure, if it is done above, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the joint to calm an abscess with heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The leg is never broken in the middle, but this happens sometimes; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it declines towards the joint, and feels great pain, and there is no relief, and sometimes it vomits blood, and opens the veins in the broken bone, and it smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and you put a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs with your hands, and subtly place it evenly in all ways as you can, so that the shape of the bone is like this; then wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and return it to its natural position on the back, and hold it firmly, and release it every hour, and if it relaxes, then hold it again; and if it needs to be released, because of corrosion or itchiness that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, do it quickly, and release it, and remove the covering, and treat it in a manner of cure; then remove the covering, and hold it firmly until it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the break of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I know that the rib fracture does not come from above but from within, and it hurts more towards the end near the spine, and it feels good when it is stretched.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you make it even, then restore it as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and tie it with a bandage, if you need to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is turning inwards, then the patient feels great pain and a kind of burning, because the bone rubs against the skin; it makes him weak and he starts to vomit a lot of blood, and this is very bad for health, and the old ones suffer greatly.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if these people whose job it is to administer meat that swells the belly, so that the fracture goes away.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, except that the warm blood comes out if it has come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let the sound come.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we should put leeches on the place, to suck out the excess, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the leeches will not attract the excesses to the place of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the place with another moist thing in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the space even, then let it be cured of the plague, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that hits the tent, then there is doubt in the patient, so one should split the bone under the torn rib, and put a tool to keep it from moving; and then one must cut the two ends of the wound, if it is big, and cure it with poultices until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses come to head, so cover them with oil and put on poultices; and cure while the head of that which it concerns to an abscess, and let rest there where it is, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break from the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes that breaks the bones of the neck, and it has not happened before; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to someone, and you do not know if he will be healed or not, take care that his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, then feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if he does not move and feels well when he is stretched out, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the disease is cured, if one applies the cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you can tell whether it is healthy or not, pay attention to whether the toes are softened, and to the accident that has happened there, and on the back there is a feeling of wind and excretion without wanting; and when it is soothed on his belly, if there is no feeling of excretion without wanting.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is soothed on his back and he tries to move, he can't.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not bother with its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come from anywhere, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward if there is an abscess, oil or beef suet on the spine so that it is calmed down; then put on one of the plasters that comfort and dry, and tie it with a string, and order the patient to rest; and don't sleep on that side where he feels pain until he is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et si certains os se désarticulent, couvrez-les avec du lambeau de peau; then break the bone, and join the two lips of the wound together, if it is large, with a stitch, then dress it with ointment, including char, until it is healthy; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called "the joint of the cow", then squeeze your pouche with your left hand, and place it equally with your right hand above the injury, then apply the plaster and the bandage, if you need to; then bind it up, and if there are any bones that have come loose, fasten them back in place, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, let there be only a small reduction at the top; then smooth it down, and set it in place at the edge of the parridge, and bring the patient pain and swelling at the site of the break.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the setting-to, is that you hold your hand over it as long as you are above the break; and know what this break is and its form; and if the break is at the top joint, then make this break equal, as long as it is in natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it leans inward, then let the patient sit with his back upright, as long as the setting-to of this break has been arranged for him.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, then put plaster on it, and then tie it with a string or a cord, and hold the break tight so that it does not move; and fit the joint with strips of cloth, as long as the place is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And order the patient to sleep on his back or side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess develops, do not scratch it, as long as the abscess is calm, and put that which we have just said before; and then return to the setting-to, and hold it tight as needed, unless there is some bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	of the dislocation of the shoulder is what lies between the collarbone and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then we restore it according to one of the two ways: one is that you take a long piece of wood, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And make two knots in the two ends, and stretch it well up, and cut the patient on a bench; then place the broken end of the arm on a long piece of wood, so that it comes to rest on the palm of the hand, and have another person hold a beam of wood behind it, then lift it up with one end resting on the palm of the hand, and put the broken end on an even surface; then make the two ends of the arm even with each other, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that you tie the patient to his bed, and bind his hand to his neck, then order the ministers that one hold what is on the break to his hand, and the others stretch out all his limbs to their parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is stronger, then hold the patient's hand away from the break, and over the break, and extend each of the ministers to his side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the shoulder blade, then you must put the patient' hand away from the break, and over the break; and likewise, if the break is on one side of the neck, you must put the hand on the other side; and likewise, if the break is on one side of the neck, you must put it lightly, without effort, as long as the break is even on top and on the neck; then make the break even, if necessary, and hold it in place, because there will be no pain.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the abscess breaks, do not hold it back for more than seven days, and put a wet cloth on the break, then dry it; then hold it in place, and the way you hold it in place is that you put plasters on the break, then tie the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest; and wrap the bandage around, and hold it in place over the shoulder, and over the arm, so that the arm is straight, unless something is holding it back, or if the bone is broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the nose does not move, use a lever, and put on the fracture a more wide and stronger lever than the others, and leave between each lever II degrees of space, and let each lever be so large that it passes III degrees of space on each side; then pull up with the levers, so as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the plaster on the fracture, more strongly and less by removing.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the levers and the pulling up, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the member broken, and you doubt the ache of the aposteme, let it be bound until seven days, as we have said; then watch each of the III days for itching that does not grow or come to the place where it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If this treatment does not work, if no such accident happens within three days or more, and the patient sleeps on their back, with their hands on their stomach; then tie the shoulder with one cotton sock of equal thickness, and check every hour during the day or night, that the shape of the limb does not move, or that the ligaments are not relaxed; if it responds to the power of medicine, and gives them the food which we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at the first layer of substance; and when they begin to improve, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset after forty days of everything; and then they should be removed and given baths and medications to treat them effectively.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if it is stiff and encrusted, it will take days or months to loosen it.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one small and one large; the small one lies next to the elbow, and the large one is above it; perhaps the large foscile breaks by itself, or the small one, or perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the healing is easy and swift; and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult and painful, more so than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small foscile is broken, then it is sufficient to extend it slightly and to make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large foscile that is broken, then it must be stretched more strongly; and extend it on one knee, and turn the hand up higher than the other limbs, and the small fingers down lower than the other fingers, and so the patient crosses his arm across himself in the middle, and the knee before him higher than the hand, that the patient feels no pain; then extend the minister's arms to the dislocated part at his hand, or at the elbow, and another minister's arms at the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then make the mirror even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are any broken pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is one that does not fit, and you cannot put it back in its place, then do so on top of the bone, as we have said above.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the breakage, I will speak about it in the single chapter of the antidote; then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if there is an obstacle to the restoration [of the bone] come the abscesses, then cover them with a cloth made of oil rosin and white wax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and I cover them from above very gently, until the abscesses are calm.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then cover the bone with cerot, and I put on the plaster of the powder from the mill with a lot of ash, because I put the splints, and it is that the splint of the breakage is closer to the top, and one more piece larger than the others; and know that there should be six splints or arms in several dispositions: whether the breakage is in one bone or in two; and drag them up above the breakage more than anywhere else, and always less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter of the antidote; and may the cloth that are on the breakage be soft and moist, and not too hard nor too rough; and may the thread, from which it is dragged, be made of linen, not too thick nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And let the limb and the ligature rest for a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you soak the limb in hot water until this itch is relieved; and let the limb rest without being restricted.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then begin the extraction again, and if the ligature is relaxed and the bone is exposed, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the joint can no longer be moved due to its being too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little bit, and leave it like that for several days until the movement returns, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the disease, then loosen the limb up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or let him sit, then put his hands on his neck, and make his neck even, and keep away from movement and turning, and sleep on his back; and know that this broken one is healed in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and to us there are few breaks, and only sometimes comes a little pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or painful, so that the patient feels a sharp pain and sits upright correctly even; then let him put his hand on an extended towel, and spread out the broken bones, and make them even by force, and put the plaster and staples, if any abscesses come, then put a staff according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in I linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks in the paregore between the belly of the plant, so make a rope of drapels, and command the patient that he estranges to his broken plant; and then he draws out with a long rope, and is its stele of both sides as much as the plant of the hand, and draws, if it comes.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks on the side, so that you put a stake above, and another behind in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and seal the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the two sides, if it's a puncture wound, then make it even, as it comes; and tie it with the plant, and if you see that you have to put a small straight stake to lift the break, so that it doesn't move; and if the break is on both sides, as in the index or one of the others, then make it even, and tie the two healthy ones together; or you tie them all together, making sure not to hurt, or you put a stake up, as though you were going to hang yourself; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of an abscess, and help whoever comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the chest bruise
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The rib bones of the chest are often bruised, and we can clearly see when they turn forward and backward; and restoration is made so that it is tied above the broken bone, and another is fixed.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister their bond to its equal part; and this is when the broken bone is inserted into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the chest, then one of the bonds extends to the hand's back, and another fixed bond fixes the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the knee, then one of the bonds extends to the back of the knee, and another bond fixes the break downward; then put the binder on the bone according to its natural shape, and then place the plaster, and the bandage, for this does not come easily.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, if he leaves it calm then returns to your work and your treatment; the time is right in some way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, wrap it in a dry cloth tightly doubled up II or III times, and leave the excess, then return the leg as far as the heel comes to the root of the ankle, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, loosing the knee joint, and let the head of the thread come up; then return to the leg and to the thigh with the bandage, then put on stakes, and put a stake on the bone of the leg; then employ the fire viciously between the leg and the thigh of drapelsou to make equal the extraction, then begin to tie III twists or IIII around the bruise; and as you go up more on the bruise, and less extract; then place II stakes that are above that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and in lier III stakes that are over, then return to the joint at the head of the thread, until you come up from the foot; and the extraction, if it does not move from its place, then let it be, then, if there is no abscess or swelling or other symptom.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to dislocation, and addresses who comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hold, so far as possible; and if one cannot, then it is necessary to split the place, and to draw it strongly; and heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the loin wounded in this way, as when the shoulder or arm is wounded; however, in this restoration made it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the loin is restored in two days, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the leg from the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	know that in the leg from the knee there is little fracture, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is a split or a fracture, and has come to all pain, and there is no pain, and this feels wrong.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et li restauration si est c'on mette igal ceu qui est rons à ses dois, tant qu'il soit assemblez mues c'on puet; puis met l'emplaistre, et i met une estele reonde, s'tu en as mestier, et l'estraint si com il convenit, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met à chescun accident ceu k'il convenit, tant qu'il soit sanez.
de la brisure de la jambe	And the restoration is that you make even that which is twisted in two, as much as it will hold together; then apply the plaster, and put a round bandage on it, if you need one, and tighten it as it should be tightened, then apply all the provisions that we have said in other breakers, such as hot poultices and others like them; also apply to each accident what suits it, until it is healed.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You should know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all similar injuries to the arm are treated in the same way as those to the arm; therefore, the restoration is done identically, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his nose is broken, turn him around.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one can see great pain, and the sight is clear; and turn back.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then order an extension, and make it even, and tie the joints evenly; however, the fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, so the extension must be lighter and less severe; and adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two long wands that color the leg on one side and the other, and are long from the ankle to the hip; then wrap them both above and below, and tie them in the middle, and at this liaison cannot descend the leg to the right or to the left, and so it is good; and no one administers two wands from the long leg, and if it is wood, and he puts the leg to ward off movement, and properly does this in the fracture or there is a wound; and moves each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; and if the cure until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the feet
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	There is no fracture at the ankle, but there is often a fracture at the foot and only once in two and never otherwise; it comes only broken with many conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a fracture at the foot, and you see these bones rise up one above the other, so put your foot on the ground as though you wanted to walk, then now place your foot on its side, where the bones are raised, then press them down again until they return to their places; then plaster it over and stir it, and place a small table of II plain boards under the stomach of the foot, then fasten it in front of the foot, then you have wrapped drapes around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if the swelling has gone down, because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s’il i a aucuns des deux brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit aux deux de la main; puis met au deux brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou deux, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun deux une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget the other things that I have said about the other breakers, as we have said; and attend to each accident as it occurs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the elbow joint
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is broken by nature in a woman, if she is made to sit enlarged, then lean her on the back of the spine, and support her with one hand; then fill the wound with cotton of nature, and put as much in it as you can; then remove the woman from the bed, and pull her spine little by little, and at that moment let the cotton out, until it comes to the entry of nature, and the bone returns with the pull; and when she urines, if the cotton comes out, and when she has finished urinating, put it back, and do this for seven days or so: the break will be healed, and she will be able to walk; take a bladder of sheep's milk, and tie a cord around the navel, and pour all the milk into nature; then blow in the cord forming, until the milk has gone inside: nature will thus heal the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	Et when the man's or woman's nose is broken, let it be set back as we have said in the femur bone; and these breaks are not hidden from him who puts his mind to it and practices it, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means many things right way of restoration: hear now.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the virile member, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and pour the virile member with it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will be healed without surgery.
de brisure avec plaie	for break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For break with wound, it is fitting that he who has broken a bone or joint or similar thing should be healed now, so that the wounds that we have spoken of by testimony may be proven true.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, if the vitriol does not come out, then you must restart restoring the broken one in the same hour, or the next day, since the pustules are not coming out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the pustules come out, and you stop restoring it until the next day, as long as the pustules are calm, and don't touch them for three days, because you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the skin surface, it is convenient that you put it at the end lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands, take this instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and whose width corresponds to the quantity of the wound; and for that one is necessary to immerse it three or four times, according to whether it is necessary to immerse it in each cure of a broken one; and be short and a little thick, so that it does not press on the limb when you work with it, and be sharp at the front, and wide in the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "pallanche", so that the curved head of the bone should be placed on top of the base of the skull; and it is to be straightened out once, until it comes back, and even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	If the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot take the bone well, then you must chop off the base of the bone until the instrument has the power to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back together as we have said, then take an appropriate instrument, or chisel or saw, at your command; then resect what has been held in the bone with roughness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is brought back together, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you make it so that it is in its natural position, then dip the wound in black vinegar, and carefully cover it; and do not put on wax or any other oil where there is oil, lest it cause pus and corruption; then administer salves when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover all around with the quantity of salve appropriate to the wound, and take good care that the wound is not stripped along with the fracture; and many such things have been done to this end, and have brought about death or corrosion on the patient sometimes; and the instrument for breaking is softer and less sharp than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will not come to pass, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, then it does not fit that you put it on splints; but wrap it up tightly, in lieu of splints, with hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two to fall bow in the wound, if it is this that you have put on all the while, and you put on an ointment healing wounds, so as ointment tetrafarmaçon and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, in the morning and at dusk, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the members be arranged in such a way that the bow does not move leichtigly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if a day passes and he cannot bear it but comes together again, and there are little pieces of bone that make it come to pass that you have to close the wound with a bandage, and all these troublesome pieces that bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if there is a fistula that has come to light or some other kind of corruption, then you must cure it according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opened on a member, as the bone of the cheek or of the shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from it, but leave it to rot; perhaps after XX or XXX days, then heal the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	And the bruises that come about with time
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	come about again after the season of the break, mostly when it is near a joint, and a ugly thing it is to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps cannot make the limbs move naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care, therefore, if we are wounded: if we administer bitter medicines, as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcacollege, ochre, and similar things; so that you do not apply any of these things alone, or all together, and confound them with wine of bitterness, or with lye or honey; and put them on a mold, and bind them well, and do not remove the bandages day after day; and then loosen them, and start a new one, until the nodules are hardened; or you press them onto a well-made piece of plaster; for the property of plaster is that it hardens all swellings on the limbs; and if the nodule has become hardened like stone, it is necessary to cut it off, if it has come to light, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after the recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone has healed, and there remains after weakness and tenderness of the members for any of these reasons: that it was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or that there were too many ligaments, and could not bring the member into its proper position; or because of a multitude of wounds; or because of great movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, so
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood multiplies within him; and give him bath, and provide him pleasure and exercise; then put poultice on the member so that the poultice attracts much nourishment, and moisten it often with warm water, until the nourishment corrects the member's shape; and return it to its natural state.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two broken limbs after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after recovery, and the bone is cracked open, and the form of the limb is ugly, but it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that we should break a limb anew, for many fools have done this in our land; such practices are blamed, and they bring about great harm and sometimes even death. However, if the nodules and torture are fresh, it is good to immerse them in warm water or soft-softing herbs are cooked, as foils of whale, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the patch is made with a healing ointment, such as well-made dyachilon, and you take the muskellaige of whale, and confound it with goose fat or oil of sise-seed, and make a patch with it; or you take greasy figs, and grind them with hay of colon, and similar medicines that soften the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is the shoulder bone moved by constant and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the member becomes stiff and hardened, as in stone, it must be opened with iron, covering up to the bone, cutting finely slightly; and put resin and study for the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is necessary now to bring back with force.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one is delayed, and the joints swell, and by chance it is reset to its place; because then it cannot be moved at all by the swelling: many times it causes spam and other pains; nevertheless, when this will happen, let the patient be made well, then let it be left, until the abscesses are calmed down; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then move it slightly, and heal every limb as the cure comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chaplets of dislocations of the shoulder until the tip.
des mandibules	teeth
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And let the jawbones be dislocated too, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: or they are a little out of place, and become a little soft; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the chest, and cause the saliva to flow from the mouth so that it cannot be held or closed, and wrap the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return by these four dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly take it to hospital, and do not delay; and in this manner that the ministers hold the head of the sick person, and squeeze a little bag of water from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands be away, to make it equal; and order the patient that he softens his jaws, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he looks at the wound evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is a broken jaw, together with the two mandibles, let him be raised with cold water and oil, until he is raised slightly; do not tarry in raising it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they have been raised evenly, and the mouth of the sick person closes well with a mollifying agent, put him on drapings soaked in oil-and-wax paste, then lightly tie them together; and let the sick person sleep on his back, and his cheeks between two pillows, so that he does not move or strain himself at all, but eat lightly, until the pains are gone, and the mandíbulales are healed and sound; and then feed him lightly, and do not try to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the mandíble is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set back in place within an hour, and are not turned to their places, so that there come fever and a usual heat, and by chance an abdominal discharge, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see that, then know that it is a loss; and many times die those to whom it has happened, in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not come out of its socket within the continuance of the arm and of the hand, and is dislocated no more than once on either side, and one can feel it well.
