Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and extends his arms; and then press it to its form with your palm, and it will return; then put on the plaster and bandage, and tie it up; and the jaw which is towards his stomach cannot be dislocated; unless so, and if it is dislocated no more than once, then set it back to its place as we have said; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and tie it up, and command to the patient that he rest as long as he is well; and in this way is also set the jaw of the shoulder when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	I understand that the shoulder can only become dislocated in three ways: either it comes off at the top of the shoulder blade; or at the top of the thigh; or sometimes it goes back towards the shoulder, but this rarely happens; and many times it becomes dislocated forward towards the arm, but this often happens to those who have a good amount of strength, because for them it means being hospitalized; and to those who have enough strength, they recover without pain and go back to their normal lives.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes it happens to some people that there is an impact or a break, and the shoulder becomes dislocated because of a hot abscess, and they think that it has become dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you need to test it out for yourself and then start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And there is an end to the dislocations when it goes down the neck, and set apart between the shoulder that is sick and that which is sound, and you will find manifest difference between them; and you will find in the chief of the shoulder a pit, and draw the neck to the table the chief of the shoulder, as though it were one egg; and the sick can not bring his hand to his nose, or make any movement; and likewise, if it is dislocated at the top, except that it is hidden, for you will see it clearly on the table; and this way of dislocation is not but to be brought back, when it is new, or when the bone is broken.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the ministers lift up the hand of the sick person, then put on them gloves without touching the shoulder, and lift up the joint by force to its place; and the ministers lift up the hand, and extend it upward, then put it down; so come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our days later, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and soft and soothing poultices are given, as an infusion of althaea and fenugrec and melilote in water, and are applied; then the patient is to be placed on his back, and a soft girdle is tied around the shoulder, neither too loose nor too tight, then the doctor takes hold of the patient's hand and pulls gently, and another doctor rubs the patient's shoulder, so that it does not move; this shoulder returns immediately, and if you do it in this way: that you bring a man who is larger than the patient; and he stands on his right side, and raises the patient's shoulder off the ground, and lifts the girdle up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another doctor pulls the patient's hand down towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so then with him nothing heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And so we will do in another way: and that is if a long stick is inserted into the earth, of which the joint should also be like a pistol, and not too big or too small; then let it be wrapped with a scarf, but that it have a drape over it, and the patient be lying on the long stick; then let his hand be extended down one side forming, and the joint will return to its place gradually; and if it does not return by all of these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick from the arms of two hands with a diameter of three fingers wide, which has the head in such a way that it can enter perfectly into the assyle, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then let him lie on the top of the stick with the scarf wrapped around it, so that the patient is not hurt, then let it be inserted into the assyle of the patient; and spread your arms up the long stick, and hold the aid on the stick, and the arm at the head of the hand, and then put the arm on a step of a ladder with a diameter of a finger wide, and let his hands be extended down, and let it be left hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done in any way, that you put upon the shoulder an equal woolen sphere, then put the plaster prepared of powder from the mill, with incense and aloes of uff, on all the shoulder and around, then remove the spine from before, and turn the tie onto the plaster, and embrace the hand at his neck, and remain your hands in that way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he suck a little, until the members are comfortable, for he will heal sooner; and then suck more after five or seven days, and move him; and if he is hardened and has not become softened, he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place because of moisture or for another reason, that you administer cauterizations to three parts, as it is placed before or with the paste of the cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it slides after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm upstairs, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are torn or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint has never been properly positioned.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the breast and the nipples, or behind, if it is made by a sudden movement, and stretching of the hands, and I administer another place; and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes greyness to the member, and late motion, so the patient often bath, as long as that greyness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated at the front and back, and does not return to its place; it is dislocated from all sides, and most obviously in front and behind, and the dislocation is not properly placed, since we can see it and feel it clearly; and dislocate according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in this way as the absces heel comes out, because if an abscess heel came out, it would be worse to reset it; and by chance cannot be reset from all sides equally, more so behind; it is more painful than other dislocations, and by chance can cause death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is done, when it is such that you can reset it, extend its hand with your two hands; and the arms are spread wide, and the hands of the patient around the neck according to the healthy side, backward and forward, and press the joint at its base together, or at the root of its palm, as long as it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, so it comes back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not come back to its place, then give it a strong extension; and it is that the two ministers extend the arm, and they tint them two ministers, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then that you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint to the joint to his hand, then oign it with any oil to soften the joint, then bottle the joint firmly, as long as it recovers; and when it is in place, then put it on a dry plaster with sheep's fat, and strain it firmly, and bend the arm at the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is secure in its place, then loosen it and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well placed, then begin again the plastering and the tying, and leave it so for some days until it is securely set. Then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint has been moved, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or put on the joint a lamb skin of fat, then leave it for a day and a night, then reset the bone, and let him enter or bathe; and when he sweats, rub the joint well, then put the skin back on, and then enter or bathe again; and do this twice or three times until it is healed; and if you see, then put on the heel of a wet horse with heated butter, and stretch it over; then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is easy to reset, more so than other joints. However, it must be returned to its place immediately, while it is still dislocated, as well as when the joint swells or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when resetting, put the injured hand on a table, and extend the fingers, and make them even, so that the palm faces the joint's alignment, and keep it extended while it heals. However, you must check that it is in the right place; then, put the patient's palm down on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, put the patient' palm down on the table, and extend the fingers to their natural alignment.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; but if not, then extract the pus from the abscess, and let it remain in this state of no return.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot set it back in place after several days, then the joint will remain twisted; and there is no benefit to the patient except that his hands are wet, and he cannot extract anything at all: then know that the nerve has been cut, or an artery; unless there is another cause, other than extracting with a gentle cautery, and perhaps nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put the poultice that we have described on it, then extract it and leave it for 5 days, then remove it and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no break, if the wet hot water, and rub until he is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are never dislocated on either side, nor at the back of the palm or the belly; then they are joined again and the dislocation is taken to the thumb as long as it revives, then hold the head of the two fingers, and tilt them towards the part where they are joined; and leave it there for a day, and then put them straight that day; and take off the bandage, if you have done so, and make it move, and tie it again; and do this often, as long as it is tight, and do the same thing when it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is well; and do the same thing, when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are never dislocated on either side, nor at the back of the palm or the belly; then they are joined again and the dislocation is taken to the thumb as long as it revives, then hold the head of the two fingers, and tilt them towards the part where they are joined; and leave it there for a day, and then put them straight that day; and take off the bandage
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there will be no cure, because the patient quickly dies.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions come without will, cannot be held, and often the members are softened, or the II cheeks or the II arms or I And often the eschinea mutates to III parts; the one who mutates behind is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward if it has come from childhood: there is no cure or healing of everything.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of curing with great words did not bring much benefit to all; but I have condensed it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilosity that comes from behind the foot before, there is no beginning or healing; and also that which comes directly on II sides, and cannot be healed but that which comes properly at the back, as I said; it is that the patient be laid face up in an equal position, and has his eyes free so that he does not get hurt; then put a log in the earth-formed head, and another under the knees, and tie a rope behind the patient, and another under the ankles; and the two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other under the knees, among the II logs; and let them be well fastened, as we have said, and let the mirer put his palms on the back-bone, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a bowl of three arms long, and cover the wall with it, and let the patient be on one side, and pour the head of the bowl over the wall, then put the middle of the bowl on the spine; and place his toes on the other head of the bowl, and press firmly until he returns to place; and if you see anything, do it with a turn that turns in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And that you stick two torches to the head of the patient with an arm long, and place the toes on the other, and have between each torch, upside down and backwards, a palm of space long; and have in each torch a turner or link, so that the torch holds firmly to the ground, so that it does not move; and between each pair of torches have a small torch turning, so that the link turns, and have two small torches of a palm long, to turn the turner; and then bind the knot that is among the torches to the turner at the head, and the other knot to the toes at the other turner, and each servant turns his turner on all the knot, and the master makes the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, so put on plaster with much egg, and then the strips, and then the wood of a tablet of three long fingers, which, purifying its place from gilly-blussity and the part of the spine healthy, then the thread of a thread, as we have said, and use subtle fattening for the patient until he is healthy; and if anything comes at the end of health, then administer softening medicines and soothing with the wood that we have said before; and never give one piece of plunk, and never does the appearance come in the posterior spine of the back, and believe that this is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, for thus should you not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches that the joints of the thigh and the shoulder come only from dislocations, not at all like the other joints; and the joint of the thigh is dislocated according to IV parties: within and without, before and behind; and most within, and little before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of his dislocations within is such that when one joins the sick leg with the sound, it is further away, and more so than the healthy genitals, and cannot double the sick knee on fire; and it is the place which is swollen hot of abscess because the head of the thigh comes here.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him whose it comes out before, is that this accident is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose it comes before are that his leg is well according to the accomplishment; nevertheless, he does not double the knee with pain, and when he is made to walk, he cannot go forward, and holds his urine back, and swells the ankle, and when he goes, he passes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that one behind, if it cannot spread its knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the hip bone is softened, and the head of the thigh is out of place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And those who have this dislocation should not be treated unless it is old, and does not cause delay according to its condition, otherwise there is no cure for it; and it only leads to death if one is presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those who have this fresh dislocation, and it is of the four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reduce the joint, and put it back in place and move it to the right and left; by chance it will come back, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not come back in this way, it is necessary that you prepare the minister very strongly, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie it to the hip with a strap; and other ministers extend their hand above and below at the same time, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains so for a while.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to put the patient on his back, in order that you may apply a cure to his back and legs, then place the bandage over the root of the thigh, and the loop which is behind the thigh, then extend the bandage upwards towards the thigh, and towards the forceps; then apply other ministers to his arms, and embrace the large loop of the thigh, and extend it towards the back: now it will return to its place; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot do this way that we have said, it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong rope, and let them hang down from the two heels and the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended twice as much as the other; then hang them upside down from the top of a post, and let them hang down two arms' length; then command one minister to embrace the root of the thigh, and let there be other ministers hanging with the patient who embrace the thigh well, for the joints now return very easily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are far away, so lay the patient down, as we said in that which concerns gimbositeit, and strap firmly the leg properly, and also the foot; then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then put one torch between the legs of the patient on the form; and plant wet flags around, so that it does not burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and let him hold the dislocation equally to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table, and press him as we said in the gimbosité, and lay the patient on his back.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are in front, so extend the leg with pain that it is on the sick angle, and according to what I said; and let the patient hold his pain by his other hand, and press him upside down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et s'il est dislocated au loin, il ne convient pas de le tirer vers l'avant, de le lever sur la terre, mais qu'il soit plutôt replacé comme lorsqu'il était déchaîné au loin, comme nous l'avons dit plus tôt en parlant du couché sur les deux hanches; et qu'il soit placé sur sa face, et que la cuisse soient étirées comme nous l'avons dit ci-dessus, et qu'on appuie sur la jointure à la table; et il sera terminé lorsque le patient étendra ses jambes, qui seront longues; alors on retire la coquille, on met le plastre, et on tire d'une bande, de sorte que la hanche ne bouge pas; et qu'il repose trois jours ou quatre, puis qu'on le change, on met le plastre dessus; et si tu vois qu'elles sont longues, on les tire comme avant, et on les laisse trois jours; puis on les change, et on fait faire du bruit aux membres jusqu'à ce qu'ils soient confortés.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the hip joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The hip joint is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward, outward, and backward; do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient that he bend his leg to his groin, and if it does not flex at the groin, knowing that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his knee between your palms, and pull them apart, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and let others extend his foot, as long as the hip returns to its place, and the signs are that he bends his leg slightly at the groin; and put the plaster on, and make him flex his leg at the groin, and join it together firmly for three days or four, then take it off; and do not work the patient to walk until his members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, then administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated, and never completely displaced inward or outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is displaced, and it is directed forward to the part where it has been displaced: let us bring it back gently with our hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is displaced from the top, so that you must make the patient sit upright, and support him by the leg, over the ankle; then bring the foot toward you with your right hand, and then back again, and then extend it upward, and blow on the foot upward; and do this twice, as we have said, in blowing and bringing it forward; if it returns, it is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place a staff firmly in the ground between his knees, and tie the blankets around, so that he does not fall; then support the leg with one minister, and others extend the foot with their hands or with the strapping; that it be held fast by the staff; then make the minister who is holding the dislocated joint at his hands, and others support the sound leg also, and the strappings should be equal, and the staff should be placed at the top between the patient's knees to hold him up while he is being extended; then put the minister who is holding the dislocation at his hands, and others support the sound leg also, and the strappings should be equal, and the staff should be placed at the top between the patient's knees to hold him up while he is being extended; then blow on the foot upward, and make the patient walk; then blow and bring it forward twice, and make him walk twice, and if it does not return, then make the patient stand, and put a staff under his feet, and support him by the arms, and make him stand, and let the minister who is holding the dislocated joint put his foot on the ground; then the other ministers should bring the sound leg and the strappings up to the same level, and the staff should be placed at the top between the patient's knees to hold him up while he is being extended.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it has hardened, put the plaster on top of it, and form the bandage, and tie the foot to the leg, and take care that the ties are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and the bandage will become loose, if the plaster is hard; then remove it after three or four days, and do not let the patient walk for four days. And if he walks before this term, it is not a sure thing that he has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come up, you must calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, you must stretch them gently before work, and it is a light thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in the back of the foot, you must make the patient sit down on a level plain or a table straight up, and place your foot on what is open from these joints, then press your foot firmly until it straightens out; and when it has healed and there is no more opening, put a board under two legs, then form the bandage, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and let the patient rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is restored, many times the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, unless you are skilled in the art and have long used it, and are compassionate and tardy, do not be bold; and use at the beginning of soothing things for an abscess, and leave the patient to God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, now restore the member to its place, so that the abscesses come; and when the member is in its place, administer drying ointments, and cure the wound, as it should be, with poultices; and if there is a fracture and small bones are out of place, then set them, and do as we have said for simple illnesses; and guard against entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cost you dear according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming and protecting yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
